- 2026-05-12 — **Bugfix: `cutlists.cabinet_id` FK retargeted to `cabinet_templates`.** The cabinet-library Cut List pill (`_cbCutListProjActHtml` in `src/cabinet-library.js:698`) and the link-to-cabinet picker (`_clLinkToCabinet` in `src/cutlist.js:4367`) both treat `cutlists.cabinet_id` as referring to a `cabinet_templates.id` — that's what `_saveCabinetToDB` persists (`src/cabinet.js:69`) and what `cbLibrary` is loaded from (`src/cabinet.js:113`). But the FK constraint on `cutlists.cabinet_id` pointed at `cabinets(id)` (the per-project instance table), so every link attempt failed with Supabase error 23503 "Key is not present in table 'cabinets'." surfacing as the "Link failed" toast at `src/cutlist.js:4400`. Single migration `supabase/migrations/20260512081913_cutlists_cabinet_id_fk_to_templates.sql` drops `cutlists_cabinet_id_fkey` and recreates it `references public.cabinet_templates(id) on delete cascade`. Applied via Supabase MCP `apply_migration`. No data migration: column stayed nullable and was NULL on every row. No code changes — every reader/writer already assumed the templates table. **SCHEMA.md § 3.12a** updated to document the `cabinet_id` column (added 2026-05-12) and the FK target. Verified live by repeating the prior-failing update with a `cabinet_templates.id` — succeeded, re-read confirmed link persisted. **Tangential**: while diagnosing, swapped the bullet-list SVG in `_CB_CUTLIST_ICON` (`src/cabinet-library.js:692`) for the saw-blade glyph that the sidebar nav-tab uses (`index.html:171`), so the Cut List pill on cabinet cards now matches the top-level Cut List tab visually.
- 2026-05-12 — **Quote / Order / Invoice number formats unified to 3-letter prefixes.** Quote `Q-NNNN` → `QUO-NNNN` (`quotes.quote_number` text col); order `NNNN` (no prefix) → `ORD-NNNN` (`orders.order_number` text col); order-PDF per-doc prefixes promoted from 2-letter `OC` / `PF` to 3-letter `ORC` / `PRO` (Tax Invoice stays `INV`). Work Order PDF keeps its `WO-` prefix but now derives the digits from `o.order_number` instead of the raw DB row id, so screen and paper agree on the number. (1) **Generation** — `_nextQuoteNumber()` (`src/quotes.js:115`) now returns `'QUO-' + ...`; `_nextOrderNumber()` (`src/orders.js:44`) now returns `'ORD-' + ...`. Both still scan trailing-digit `match(/(\d+)/)` of existing values, so they keep working through the legacy→new transition. (2) **PDF builders** — `src/cutlist.js:2226` (Quote PDF header) now uses `q.quote_number || ('QUO-' + id.padStart(4,'0'))`; `_buildOrderDocPDF` `refNum` (`src/cutlist.js:2554`) strips `ORD-` so the per-doc 3-letter prefix replaces it; `cfg.order_confirmation.prefix` `'OC'` → `'ORC'`; `cfg.proforma.prefix` `'PF'` → `'PRO'`; `cfg.invoice.prefix` unchanged. Work Order PDF (`src/cutlist.js:2469`) derives `woRef` from `o.order_number`. The Tax Invoice closing-line `'Please reference #INV-' + refNum + ' on remittance.'` is unchanged because INV is unchanged. (3) **Display + editor** — every fallback site that previously synthesised `'Q-' + id.padStart(4,'0')` now produces `'QUO-' + ...` (quotes.js card title fallback, dashboard.js quote pill, quotes.js HTML print view title, suggest list filter regex, "Start new quote" suggest text); same pattern for orders (orders.js card / editor / suggest, dashboard.js order pill, dashboard.js schedule numberLabel, schedule.js numberLabel, cabinet-render.js editing-order banner). Quote editor input strip regex broadened from `/^Q-/i` to `/^(QUO|Q)-/i` so legacy `Q-NNNN` rows still display as bare digits in the input until the migration runs. Order editor input gains a strip-on-display + prepend-on-save pair mirroring how quotes already worked (`po-order-number` value sanitised through `String(orderNumFull).replace(/^ORD-/i, '')` for display; both `createOrderFromEditor` and `saveOrderEditor` write `'ORD-' + onRaw.replace(/^ORD-/i,'')`). The "From Quote" chip on the order editor (`src/orders.js:392`) now uses `fromQuote.quote_number` with `QUO-` fallback. (4) **Save normalization** — `createQuoteFromEditor` and `saveQuoteEditor` (quotes.js:1561 + 1606) now normalize via `'QUO-' + qnRaw.replace(/^(QUO|Q)-/i, '')` so saving an existing legacy `Q-NNNN` quote migrates that single row to `QUO-NNNN`; orders side mirrors this. (5) **Migrate.js** — legacy LS quote-import (`migrate.js:444`) also normalizes incoming `quoteNum` to the new prefix. (6) **Migration** — `supabase/migrations/20260512175008_renumber_prefixes.sql` rewrites stored values: `UPDATE quotes SET quote_number = 'QUO-' || regexp_replace(quote_number, '^Q-', '', 'i') WHERE quote_number ~* '^Q-';` and `UPDATE orders SET order_number = 'ORD-' || order_number WHERE order_number IS NOT NULL AND order_number !~* '^ORD-';`. **MCP `apply_migration` was blocked by harness permissions**; user to apply via Supabase SQL editor. Code is migration-tolerant: pre-migration the display paths show whatever's stored (legacy `Q-` / bare digits) but every new entry, every save, and every PDF render uses the new format. `npm run typecheck` clean. - 2026-05-13 — **F7: Cabinet Library sub-tab gets its own sidebar gate — standalone, out-of-client template workflow.** `#panel-cabinet` previously had two main-area sub-tabs (Quote Builder, Cabinet Library) but a single shared sidebar gated on `_cbCurrentClientId`, forcing the user to pick a client before they could touch the library. `renderCBPanel()` worked around this by auto-flipping to the Library sub-tab whenever no client was selected (`src/cabinet-render.js:211-213`), but the sidebar still showed the client-picker empty state — the Library was effectively gated. - 2026-05-15 — **Sentry error tracking wired — P.3 (DSN-gated, inert until a Sentry account exists).** Implements PLAN.md P.3 / locked decision D.5. Plan: `~/.claude/plans/set-up-sentry-dynamic-boot.md`. Installed `@sentry/browser` (^10.53.1, dependency) + `@sentry/vite-plugin` (^5.3.0, devDependency). **(1) Init** — `src/main.js` imports `* as Sentry from '@sentry/browser'` and calls `Sentry.init({ dsn, environment: import.meta.env.MODE })` at the very top, before the existing Supabase env-var check, so a missing-key `throw` is also captured. Init is gated on `import.meta.env.VITE_SENTRY_DSN` — with no DSN the SDK stays uninitialized, `Sentry.init` tree-shakes out of the build (Vite inlines the env read as `undefined`), and every `Sentry.*` call is a safe no-op, so dev and pre-account builds run untouched. `window.Sentry = Sentry` is assigned unconditionally, mirroring the existing `window.supabase` / `window.jspdf` bridge so the 27 classic `<script defer>` files can call `window.Sentry.captureException(...)` directly. **Error tracking only** — no Tracing/Replay/Profiling integrations added (none are default in `@sentry/browser`), keeping Sentry's footprint ~30 KB gz; the default `globalHandlers` integration auto-hooks `window.onerror` + unhandledrejection, so uncaught errors from every classic script are captured without per-file wiring. **(2) User context** — `src/app.js` `onAuthStateChange` listener calls `window.Sentry.setUser({ id: session.user.id, email: session.user.email })` on session and `setUser(null)` on sign-out. **Decision**: user context = id + email (chosen 2026-05-15); Sentry's `sendDefaultPii` stays at its default `false`, so nothing beyond id+email is attached. **(3) Types** — `src/globals.d.ts` declares `Window.Sentry: typeof import('@sentry/browser')` beside the supabase/jspdf bridge globals so `tsc` stays clean. **(4) Source maps / releases** — `vite.config.mjs` adds `sentryVitePlugin({ org, project, authToken, disable: !process.env.SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN })`; `build.sourcemap` was already `true`. `disable` makes the plugin a no-op whenever `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN` is absent, so local `npm run build` and pre-secret CI runs never fail or attempt an upload. Note: only `main.js` is bundled/minified by Vite — the 27 domain scripts are copied verbatim to `dist/src/` (unminified, traces already readable), so the plugin's main value is release/commit grouping plus de-minified `main.js` traces. **(5) Build env** — the build runs in GitHub Actions, not Cloudflare (`wrangler pages deploy dist` only uploads the prebuilt `dist/`), so build-time env lives in `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` alongside `VITE_SUPABASE_*`. Added a commented scaffold there for `VITE_SENTRY_DSN` / `SENTRY_ORG` / `SENTRY_PROJECT` / `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`; `.env.example` documents all four (the DSN is publishable; the three `SENTRY_*` build vars are not `VITE_`-prefixed and must never reach the client). **Pending user actions** (P.3 sub-steps left ⬜): create the Sentry project (Browser JavaScript platform), fill the DSN/org/project into `deploy.yml`, add `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN` as a GitHub Actions repo secret, set up email alerts. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; `npm run build` succeeds with the vite-plugin silently no-op'd (no token) and source maps emitted, Sentry confirmed in the bundle; `npm run dev` boots with zero console warnings/errors; in the page `window.Sentry` is an object exposing `captureException`/`setUser`/`init`, `getClient()` is undefined (init correctly skipped with no DSN), and `captureException`/`setUser` no-op without throwing.
- 2026-05-15 — **PostHog product analytics wired — C.5 (key-gated, inert until a PostHog account exists).** Implements the PostHog half of PLAN.md C.5 / locked decision D.4. Plan: `~/.claude/plans/set-up-posthog-typed-grove.md`. Installed `posthog-js` (^1.373.4, dependency). **(1) Init** — `src/main.js` imports the `posthog-js` default export and calls `posthog.init(key, {...})` **only when `import.meta.env.VITE_POSTHOG_KEY` is set**; with no key the SDK never initialises and `window.posthog` stays `undefined`. The key-presence check IS the dev gate — a dev `.env.local` simply omits the key, so dev traffic never reaches prod analytics. Unlike the Supabase keys, a missing PostHog key never `throw`s (the block is a plain `if (key) {…}`, no erroring `else`). Config: `api_host` from `VITE_POSTHOG_HOST` (default `https://eu.i.posthog.com` — **EU region**, chosen this session), `person_profiles: 'identified_only'`, autocapture + pageview on, session replay enabled with **no masking** (`maskAllInputs: false`, chosen this session — password inputs are still force-masked by PostHog); autocapture + replay both stay server-toggleable from the PostHog dashboard. `window.posthog = posthog` is assigned only inside the `if` block, so the wrapper guards below genuinely gate. **(2) Wrapper module** — new classic file `src/analytics.js` (19th `<script defer>`, loaded right after `src/stripe.js`) exposes no-op-safe globals `_track(event, props)`, `_identifyUser(session)`, `_resetAnalytics()`, each guarding `window.posthog` so call sites are unconditional. `_track` auto-attaches a `plan` property (`free`/`pro`, from `isPro()`) to every event. **(3) Event model — generic, not per-entity** (decided this session for funnel flexibility): one `library_item_created` event covers all six libraries (`library` ∈ clients/quotes/orders/cutlists/stock/cabinet_templates, the `FREE_LIMITS` keys) with `library` + `item_id` + `source` props; one `pdf_created` event covers all five PDF types (`type` ∈ quote/stock_list/work_order/order_document/cutlist). A PostHog funnel can show "any library item → any PDF" directly, or filter by property for the entity-specific funnel — no event proliferation, no separate `first_*` events (PostHog funnels are first-occurrence per user natively). Other events: `user_signed_up`, `user_logged_in`, `free_tier_limit_hit` (`library`, `current_count`), `upgrade_clicked` (`billing_cycle`), `section_viewed` (`section`); plus `identify` on auth-state-change and `reset` on sign-out. PLAN.md C.5's original "first project created" funnel step is obsolete — the `projects` entity was retired (F6); cut-list creation is the analog and flows through `library_item_created` with `library:'cutlists'`. **(4) Call sites** — `library_item_created` fires from the real create path of each library (`createClient`, `createQuoteFromEditor`, `createOrderFromEditor` + `convertQuoteToOrder` + `cbCreateOrderFromDraft`, `_clStartNewCutlist` + `_clNewCabinetLinkedCutlist`, `addStockItem`, `_saveCabinetToDB`); the empty draft-placeholder paths (`_qStartNewQuote`/`_oStartNewOrder`) are deliberately NOT wired so abandoned drafts don't inflate the metric. `pdf_created` fires inside each `_build*PDF` chokepoint in `cutlist.js` (covers every caller). `free_tier_limit_hit` fires in `_enforceFreeLimit` (one edit covers all libraries); `upgrade_clicked` in `_handleUpgradeClick`; `section_viewed` in `switchSection`. **`identify` runs in `onAuthStateChange` AFTER `await loadAllData()`** so `_subscription`/`isPro()` is loaded — otherwise the person is permanently mis-tagged `plan:'free'`. **(5) Types** — `src/globals.d.ts` declares `Window.posthog?: typeof import('posthog-js').default` (mirrors the Sentry bridge line). `.env.example` documents `VITE_POSTHOG_KEY` + `VITE_POSTHOG_HOST`. **Decision: npm + bridge, not a CDN snippet** — overrides C.5's loose "install snippet" wording, for consistency with the Supabase/jsPDF/Sentry bridge and real TS types. **Out of scope**: Cloudflare Web Analytics + Google Search Console (rest of C.5, still ⬜). **Pending user actions**: create the PostHog project (EU region), put `VITE_POSTHOG_KEY` into `.github/workflows/deploy.yml` + Cloudflare Pages env, build the funnels in the PostHog dashboard. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; `npm run build` succeeds with the key absent (proves no throw) — `dist/src/analytics.js` copied, `dist/index.html` carries the tag, `posthog-js` in the bundle; `npm run dev` reload — app boots with zero console errors, `window.posthog` is `undefined` (dev gate), `_track`/`_identifyUser`/`_resetAnalytics` are defined and no-op without throwing. Live-event confirmation deferred — needs the user's real PostHog key.

A logged-out visitor now sees the whole app pre-seeded with a realistic dataset (5 clients / quotes / orders / cutlists / cabinet templates, 10 stock items) and can explore every tab; trying to *save* opens a sign-in prompt. **Mechanism**: new `src/demo.js` holds the static seed + `_demoSelect` (resolves a `_DBBuilder` against the seed) + `_demoBlockWrite`; `src/db.js`'s `_DBBuilder.then()` branches on `window._demoMode` — reads served from the seed, writes blocked. No engine change — `_wtDrawSpot` already draws the ring from one element's `getBoundingClientRect()`, so a wrapper target Just Works. - 2026-05-17 — **Returning free users get the Pro CTA once per browser session.** A signed-in free user who has already completed the first-run guided tour now sees just the final Pro CTA — not the whole tour — once per browser session; the full tour stays first-login-only. **Mechanism** (`src/walkthrough.js`): new `_wtStartCta()` opens the overlay directly on the final `showPricing` step, and a new module flag `_wtCtaOnly` marks the mode so it behaves as a standalone modal rather than a tour — `_wtApplyContext` skips the `switchSection` / `_wtGateSection` calls, `_wtClose` skips the dismissal persistence and the "land on Dashboard" `switchSection`, and `_wtNext` / `_wtBack` collapse to single-step so Back and ← can't step out of the CTA into the middle of the tour. - 2026-05-18 — **Two post-launch bug fixes: client-delete cascade, and Cabinet Builder quotes are no longer hidden.** **(1) Client delete cascade** (`src/clients.js`): `removeClient` deleted only the `clients` row, orphaning that client's quotes, orders and cut lists. It now removes all of them — cut lists first (`cutlists.quote_id` → `quotes` is `ON DELETE SET NULL`, so `removeClient` deletes `cutlists` by the client's quote ids before the quotes go), then `orders` and `quotes` (`quote_lines` / `order_lines` and cut-list child rows cascade at the DB level), then the client row — pruning the in-memory `quotes` / `orders` arrays and `_cutListsByClient`; on a DB error it toasts and aborts. New `_confirmRemoveClient(id)` builds the confirm warning ("Delete <b>Name</b> and permanently remove N quotes, M orders and K cut lists? This cannot be undone." — quote/order counts from memory, cut-list count via a live query). Pre-existing bug noted but left untouched: `_loadCutListsByClient` still selects a dropped `cutlists.client_id` column, so `_cutListsByClient` is always empty and the Clients-card cut-list section never renders. **(2) Cabinet Builder hidden-draft model removed** (`src/cabinet.js`, `src/quotes.js`): the builder autosaved into a `status:'designing'` quote that `_isDraftQuote` hid from the Quotes tab, client cards, dashboard and CSV export — so a quote built in the Cabinet Builder appeared nowhere except via "Go to Quote". Per user decision the hidden state is removed: `_findOrCreateDraftQuote` now creates a normal `status:'draft'` quote (find step dropped); `_loadCBClientById` creates it eagerly when a client is picked for a new quote, enforces the free-tier quote cap, and adopts it via `cbEditingQuoteId` (persisted to `pc_cb_editing_quote_id`); the `_syncCBLinesToDB` else-branch does the same as a self-healing fallback, routing through `_syncCBLinesToQuote`. A Cabinet Builder quote is now a first-class draft — visible everywhere immediately and counted toward the 5-quote free cap. `_isDraftQuote` is kept only to hide any pre-existing `'designing'` / `[CB_DRAFT]` rows. **Diverges from** `item-2-cabinet-quote-unification.md` Phase 2 ("Quotes tab shows formal non-draft quotes only") — the draft/snapshot split is collapsed. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` + `npm run build` clean; dev-preview end-to-end — the new-quote flow creates a `status:'draft'` quote that renders in the Quotes tab ("Draft (1)") and on the client card ("1 quote · QUO-0065 Draft"); deleting the client shows the cascade warning and removes client + quote from the in-memory arrays and the DB (re-queried — zero orphans).

- 2026-05-18 — **Manage Subscription popup shows the live offer price + price-increase date.** The active-subscription popup (`_openManagePopupActive`, `src/stripe.js`) hard-coded `$35/mo` / `$300/yr`, so every subscriber on the launch coupon ($25/mo for the first 6 months then $35/mo, auto-applied at checkout via `STRIPE_COUPON_MONTHLY_LAUNCH`) saw the standard price, not what they actually pay. The discount lives only in Stripe — the `subscriptions` table mirrors plan/status/period, never the coupon. **Decision — fetch live on popup-open, not mirror via the webhook**: the alternative (add discount columns + have `stripe-webhook` write them) needs a migration and only populates on a subscriber's *next* Stripe event, so existing subscribers would show stale/empty data until then (a backfill); a live read is accurate for everyone immediately, needs no migration, and can't go stale. **New `stripe-subscription` edge function** (`supabase/functions/stripe-subscription/`) — authenticates the caller's Supabase JWT, looks up their `stripe_subscription_id`, retrieves the subscription with `expand:['discounts']`, and returns `{currency, interval, standardAmount, currentAmount, discountEnd}` (minor units; `currentAmount` = standard with the coupon's `percent_off`/`amount_off` applied; `discountEnd` from `discount.end`). Mirrors `stripe-portal`'s auth/CORS conventions; no new secrets. **Client** — `_openManagePopupActive` renders the price card with a "Loading…" placeholder (`#ms-price-line`) plus a hidden `#ms-increase-line`, then fires `_fillManageSubscriptionPricing`: on success it shows the discounted price and, when a dated discount is active, an "Increases to $35/mo on &lt;date&gt;" line; on failure or no active discount it falls back to the static plan price. New helpers `_loadSubscriptionPricing` (authed fetch) and `_fmtSubscriptionPrice` (forces the en-US locale so USD renders `$` not `US$`; shows 2 decimals only for non-whole amounts). No schema change. **Deployed** to the live project (version 1, `verify_jwt: true`, no new secrets) and smoke-tested (OPTIONS preflight 204 + CORS, unauthenticated POST 401); the popup reads real pricing once the frontend ships. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview — formatter ($25/mo, $300/yr, $35.50/mo, £25/mo), fallback ("$35/mo", no increase line), stubbed-discount render ("$25/mo" + "Increases to $35/mo on 18/11/2026"), and no-discount render (increase line hidden) all confirmed.
- 2026-05-18 — **Security + load review — five fixes (items 1, 2, 5, 6, 10 of 12).** A security/load review flagged 12 issues; this batch actions five. Plan: `~/.claude/plans/do-1-2-5-only-mask-lovely-snail.md`. **(#1 N+1)** `_hydrateQuoteTotals` / `_hydrateOrderLines` (`src/quotes.js`) fetched `quote_lines` / `order_lines` once per quote/order on every boot (and hourly token refresh). Both rewritten to one batched `.in()` query each, grouped by parent id in memory; `q._lines` / `q._totals` / `o._lines` populated identically to before (`_lineSubtotal` reused for the totals math; `quoteTotalsFromLines` / `orderTotalsFromLines` / `_refreshQuoteTotals` kept unchanged for single-record post-edit refreshes). Dev-preview verified — a 4-order account now issues one `order_lines?order_id=in.(…)` request, was four. **(#2 DB performance)** migration `20260518150000_perf_indexes_and_rls_initplan.sql` (applied via Supabase MCP): adds 10 missing FK covering indexes (`user_id` on cabinet_hardware/clients/edge_bands/order_lines/pieces/quote_lines/quotes/sheets; `client_id` on orders/quotes) and rewrites all 61 RLS policies that called `auth.uid()` per row to `(select auth.uid())` — the InitPlan optimisation, semantically identical (same rows), evaluated once per query. `get_advisors` performance: the `auth_rls_initplan` ×57 and `unindexed_foreign_keys` ×10 lints all cleared; only INFO `unused_index` notices remain (expected on a near-empty DB — do not drop). SCHEMA.md § 4 updated to the `(select auth.uid())` form. **(#5 PostHog privacy)** `src/main.js` session-recording config gains `maskTextSelector` for the six Business Info fields (`#biz-name/#biz-phone/#biz-email/#biz-address/#biz-abn/#biz-bank-details`) — the owner's own company PII + bank/payment details. **Decision — business-info fields only**: per user scope choice, client data and pricing are deliberately NOT masked. **(#10 build)** `vite.config.mjs` — `copyClassicScriptsPlugin` now minifies each `src/*.js` through `esbuild.transformSync` before writing to `dist/src/` (production previously served the full commented source). **Decision — `minifyIdentifiers: false`**: the classic scripts share state through the global lexical environment, so identifier mangling would rename cross-file globals and break the app; only `minifyWhitespace` + `minifySyntax` are applied — strips all comments, ~35% smaller, global names intact. **Decision — classic-script source maps dropped (not uploaded to Sentry)**: the hand-copied `src/*.js` bypass Rollup, so they never receive the Sentry plugin's debug-ID injection — feeding their maps to Sentry is not a clean config change. They ship minified without maps; identifiers are preserved so Sentry frames keep real function names (only line numbers are lost). `build.sourcemap` set to `'hidden'`; a new `stripSourceMapsPlugin` deletes every `dist/**/*.map` in `closeBundle` (after the Sentry plugin's `writeBundle` upload), so the Vite-bundle maps still upload to Sentry but no `.map` ever ships — and it is independent of `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`, so maps are stripped even when Sentry is disabled. **(#6 leaked-password protection)** — pending manual step: enable it in the Supabase dashboard (Authentication → password settings); no MCP tool exposes the auth config. **Out of scope** (the other 7 review items — XSS escaping, CSP/security headers, list pagination, DB-side IDs, server-side free-tier enforcement) deferred. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` + `npm run build` clean; dev preview — batched `.in()` requests confirmed, signed-in hydration correct; the built/minified app booted on `npm run preview` and navigated every tab with zero console errors; `find dist -name '*.map'` empty.
- 2026-05-18 — **Landscape-mode usability — pane scroll chain + touch-resizable sidebars.** Plan: `~/.claude/plans/optimize-for-mobile-streamed-bonbon.md`. Scoped by the user to making the existing desktop layout *usable on a phone/tablet in landscape* with no visual redesign — two behaviour-only fixes, both inert when the viewport is tall/wide enough. **(1) Flex scroll chain** — `body` is a bounded `height:100vh` flex column and each pane nests an `overflow:auto` scroll container (`.sidebar-scroll` / `.main-scroll` / `.cl-scroll`), but no layout element set `min-height:0`. A flex item defaults to `min-height:auto`, so on a short landscape viewport the scroll container expanded to content height instead of staying bounded — its `overflow:auto` never engaged and the parent's `overflow:hidden` simply clipped the bottom, leaving content unreachable. Added one consolidated `styles.css` rule setting `min-height:0; min-width:0` on the whole pane chain — `.app-body`, `.section-panel`, `.sidebar`, `.sidebar-scroll`, `.main-content`, `.main-scroll`, `.cl-left`, `.cl-right`, `.cl-scroll`, `.sched-sidebar`, `.sched-sidebar-body`, plus the inline-styled `flex:1` wrappers `#cab-view-builder` / `#cb-sidebar-builder` / `#cb-sidebar-library` / `#schedule-main` (their inline `style` never declares `min-height`, so the rule applies without a specificity conflict). Invisible when content fits; only turns a clipped pane into a scrollable one. One related fix surfaced in verification — the Cabinet Builder's empty-state client picker renders into `#cb-context`, a plain block *outside* any scroll container, so on a short viewport it clipped (~25px at 844×390) with no way to scroll; `#cb-sidebar-builder`'s inline `overflow:hidden` (`index.html`) was changed to `overflow-y:auto;overflow-x:hidden` so the wrapper itself scrolls when the picker overflows. In-project the `flex:1` `#cb-sidebar` scroller absorbs all overflow, so the wrapper never shows a scrollbar there. **(2) Touch-resizable sidebars** — `_initSidebarResize` (`src/ui.js`) already used Pointer Events, but the handle was blocked by CSS: `@media (max-width:768px){ .resize-handle{display:none} }` removed it on smaller landscape phones, and with no `touch-action` a touch-drag on a visible handle was hijacked as a page pan. Deleted the 768px hide rule, added `touch-action:none` to `.resize-handle`, and widened the invisible `::after` hit area under `@media (pointer:coarse)` for fingers (no visual change — the handle itself is a 4px transparent strip). The `pointermove` handler now also clamps the max width to `window.innerWidth − 140` so the sidebar can't be dragged wide enough to hide the main viewer on a narrow screen. **Out of scope** (deliberate): no layout redesign — no drill-in / pane-stacking / bottom nav, the two-pane layout is unchanged per "visually stay the same"; iOS zoom-on-focus left alone (inputs are 12–13px, fixing it means a visible bump to 16px). A landscape-usability precursor to the full PLAN.md M.1 responsive pass, which stays open. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview at a landscape phone size (844×390) — every tab's sidebar and main viewer scroll to the bottom with nothing clipped, the resize handle drags via touch and clamps; re-checked at 1440×900 for zero visual change.
- 2026-05-18 — **`100vh` → `100dvh` for mobile viewport accuracy.** Follow-up to the landscape entry above. Three `styles.css` rules used `vh` — `body { height }`, `.account-dropdown { max-height: calc(100vh - 80px) }`, `.popup-modal { max-height: 90vh }` — and `vh` on mobile is the *bar-hidden* viewport (taller than what's visible), so the app shell, the header dropdown, and popups could extend behind the browser URL bar. All three switched to `dvh` (dynamic viewport height) so they track the actually-visible area as the URL bar shows/hides. `vw` (popup widths) left alone — horizontal chrome doesn't move. Identical to `vh` on desktop and in the fixed-viewport dev preview (`body` computed 390px = viewport, no regression); the gain only shows on a real mobile browser. `dvh` is supported everywhere current (iOS Safari 15.4+, Chrome 108+), so no `vh` fallback line.
- 2026-05-18 — **Mobile/tablet opening notice — once-per-visit desktop-first advisory.** Plan: `~/.claude/plans/add-an-opening-message-staged-flute.md`. A touch-device visitor now gets a one-time dismissible notice on app load — "Best viewed on a computer": the app isn't fully mobile-optimised yet, use a desktop/laptop for the full experience, limited use is possible on a phone/tablet in landscape. **Informational, not a hard block** — the app stays usable behind it. **New `src/mobile-notice.js`** (`<script defer>` before `walkthrough.js`): `_pcIsTouchDevice()` returns `window.matchMedia('(hover: none) and (pointer: coarse)').matches` — true for phones + tablets, false for desktops/laptops including touchscreen laptops (their primary pointer is `fine`); `_pcMaybeShowMobileNotice()` no-ops on desktop or when `sessionStorage['pc_mobile_notice_seen']` is set, otherwise sets the flag and appends a self-contained inline-styled overlay (modelled on `ui.js`'s `_confirm()` — reuses the `popupFadeIn`/`popupSlideIn` keyframes + theme vars, **no new CSS**) at **z-index 10000**, above the walkthrough overlay (~9760) and below toasts (99999). Backdrop-click and the "Continue anyway" button both dismiss. **Decisions (confirmed with the user before execution)**: (1) frequency = once per *visit* — a `sessionStorage` gate, re-shows next session, not once-ever; (2) the guided walkthrough still runs — the notice layers *above* the auto-started tour and the walkthrough is revealed underneath on dismiss (not suppressed on mobile); (3) scope = phones *and* tablets. **Hook**: a single line at the top of `_wtMaybeAutoStart()` (`src/walkthrough.js`) calls `window._pcMaybeShowMobileNotice()` — the existing onboarding entry gate, run after `_showApp()` in both boot branches — with no early return, so the tour proceeds. `src/globals.d.ts` declares the two `window` globals. No schema change. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview — `_pcIsTouchDevice()` returns `false` on desktop (notice no-ops, desktop users never interrupted); with the touch media query stubbed, the overlay renders centred at 375px wide with the correct copy + amber button at z-index 10000, the button and a backdrop click both dismiss it, and a second `_pcMaybeShowMobileNotice()` call no-ops while the session flag is set but shows again once cleared.
- 2026-05-18 — **Guided walkthrough — mobile landscape support.** The onboarding spotlight tour (`src/walkthrough.js`) is desktop-first: it anchors a 336px tooltip *beside* each highlighted element and centres the welcome / pricing modals. On a phone both broke — in portrait there is no room beside a target so `_wtPlaceTooltip` clamped the tooltip on top of what it pointed at, and `.wt-center` (`overflow:hidden`, no `max-height`) overflowed a short viewport, clipping the pricing CTA's "Continue free" exit button off-screen (no arrow keys on touch → the user could be trapped). **Decisions (confirmed with the user)**: (1) scope = the walkthrough overlay only — the app's non-reflowing section panels are a separate, larger effort and stay out of scope; (2) on a phone the tour runs **landscape only**, visually identical to desktop (no bottom-sheet redesign — a landscape phone ≈844px+ is wide enough for the existing placement); (3) touch navigation = tap the **right/left half of the screen** to step forward/back, replacing the arrow keys touch devices lack. **(1) Landscape gate** — new `_wtIsPortraitBlocked()` (`(orientation:portrait) and (max-width:767px) and (pointer:coarse)` — one `matchMedia`, gated on a coarse pointer so a narrow desktop window is never affected) and `_wtDrawRotatePrompt()` (a `.wt-center`-based "Rotate your device" card — circular rotate icon, heading, body, "Skip tour" button). `_wtRender` shows the rotate prompt instead of a step when blocked, keeping `_wtCurrent` so turning the device re-renders the same step; the standalone session CTA (`_wtCtaOnly`) is exempt — a centred scrollable modal that works in portrait. New `orientationchange` listeners registered alongside the existing `resize` in `_wtRunStart`/`_wtStartCta` and removed in `_wtClose`; both drive the rotate-prompt ↔ step swap. **(2) Centred modals scroll** — `styles.css` `.wt-center` swaps `overflow:hidden` for `overflow:hidden auto` and adds `max-height:calc(100dvh - 24px)` (with a `100vh` fallback line). Universal — only engages when content exceeds the viewport height (short landscape phones), so desktop is visually unchanged; the welcome and pricing modals now cap to the viewport and scroll internally, so the CTA's exit button is always reachable. New `.wt-rotate-icon` rule (circular accent badge). **(3) Touch navigation** — `_wtOverlayClick` gains tap-to-step after the existing `data-wt-act` button handling: on a coarse pointer, a tap on the dimmed backdrop (not on the tooltip / centre card / rotate prompt) advances when `clientX > innerWidth/2`, else goes back. Desktop (fine pointer) is unaffected — arrow keys + buttons only. **(4) Device-aware copy** — the welcome step's body dropped its hard-coded "use the arrow keys on your keyboard" clause; `_wtCenterPreviewHTML` now appends a `matchMedia('(pointer: coarse)')`-chosen hint — tap-zone wording on touch, arrow-keys wording otherwise. Complements `mobile-notice.js`'s once-per-session "rotate to landscape" advisory (which advises; the walkthrough enforces landscape for the tour itself). No schema change. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview — desktop: welcome + 4-column CTA render unchanged, no clipping (`scrollHeight===clientHeight`), arrow-keys hint shown; landscape phone (844×390): welcome and CTA modals cap at `calc(100dvh-24px)`=366px and scroll internally with "Continue free" reachable after scroll, spot-step tooltip places below the spotlit nav bar fully in-viewport; portrait (390×844): `_wtDrawRotatePrompt()` renders the rotate card centred and fully in-viewport (`_wtIsPortraitBlocked()`'s portrait + max-width terms confirmed true — the `pointer:coarse` term, and so the auto-gate and tap navigation, needs a real touch device the desktop preview can't emulate).
- 2026-05-18 — **Portrait phones — horizontal-scroll the desktop layout instead of crushing it.** Follow-up to the landscape entries above. In portrait the two-pane layout didn't overflow, it *crushed*: the fixed-width sidebar held its width and `.main-content` (`flex:1; min-width:0`) squeezed to ~80px (the Cut List was worse — `.cl-left`'s 400px `min-width` overflowed the panel and `.cl-right` collapsed to 0). New `styles.css` media query `@media (orientation: portrait) and (max-width: 600px)` — phones held upright only; tablets (≥744px in portrait) and every landscape viewport are excluded — sets `.app-body { overflow-x: auto; justify-content: flex-start }` (`flex-start` so the panel's left edge stays scroll-reachable; `center` would strand it) and `.section-panel.active { min-width: 840px }`, so the full desktop two-pane layout holds at 840px and the body pans horizontally. Dashboard (single-pane) pans too — user's choice, for one consistent behaviour across tabs. 840px leaves every section a usable main pane (cabinet 400 / cutlist 360 / quote+order 480 / clients+stock 530 / schedule 620 / dashboard 840). `_initSidebarResize`'s `pointermove` (`src/ui.js`) now skips the `innerWidth − 140` viewport clamp when that same media query matches — in portrait-scroll mode a wide sidebar stays reachable by panning, so the clamp (which exists to stop the sidebar hiding the viewer on a *non-scrolling* landscape screen) is counterproductive there. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview at 390×844 portrait — all 8 tabs hold the 840px panel and `.app-body` scrolls 450px to reveal it, the resize handle drags to its full `data-max` (cutlist 680, not viewport-capped); re-checked at 844×390 landscape — panel back to 844, no horizontal scroll, `.app-body` overflow/justify untouched.
- 2026-05-18 — **Landscape chrome auto-collapse — demo banner + nav-tab bar slide away on scroll.** Follow-up to the mobile walkthrough work. On a short landscape phone (~390px tall) the `body` flex column's fixed chrome — `header` (56px) + `#demo-banner` (~36px, demo/guest only) + `.nav-tabs-wrap` (~45px) — left only ~250px for content. The demo banner + nav-tab bar now collapse when a content pane is scrolled down and restore on scroll up, handing the freed height to `.app-body` (flex:1). The top header stays put — per the user, "just the tab bar and demo bar". **CSS** (`styles.css`): `#demo-banner, .nav-tabs-wrap` get `max-height: 80px` (an inert cap — real content is ~36/45px) plus a `max-height`/`padding`/`opacity` transition; `body.chrome-collapsed #demo-banner, body.chrome-collapsed .nav-tabs-wrap` sets `max-height: 0; padding: 0; opacity: 0; overflow: hidden`. **Decision — explicit `padding: 0` in the collapsed rule**: the demo banner's `padding: 7px 16px` survived `max-height: 0` (content-box — the cap zeroes content height, not padding), leaving a 14px residue confirmed in the preview; zeroing the padding (and transitioning it) collapses it fully. The nav-tab bar has no padding, so it is a no-op there. **JS** (`src/ui.js`): new `_initChromeCollapse()` registers one capture-phase `scroll` listener on `document` — scroll events don't bubble, so the capture phase catches scrolling in any pane (`.sidebar-scroll` / `.main-scroll` / `.cl-scroll`) with a single listener; it tracks each scroller's last `scrollTop` in a `WeakMap` and toggles `body.chrome-collapsed` by direction (down → collapse; up, or `scrollTop ≤ 6` → restore), rAF-throttled. **Gating**: the handler early-returns unless `matchMedia('(pointer: coarse)').matches`, so desktop (fine pointer) is never affected — and the CSS only reacts to the class, so it is inert on desktop regardless. It also early-returns while `window._wtActive` (the guided tour spotlights the nav tabs — keep them shown), and an `orientationchange` listener resets to the expanded state. No schema change. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview at a landscape phone size (844×390) — with transitions momentarily disabled for an exact read, toggling `body.chrome-collapsed` collapses `#demo-banner` 36→0 and `.nav-tabs-wrap` 45→0, `.app-body` grows 254→334 (≈80px, ~31% more content height) and starts flush under the 56px header; collapsed-state screenshot confirmed. The scroll-direction trigger is JS-gated to coarse pointers, which the desktop preview can't emulate — verified by code; live confirmation needs a real touch device.
- 2026-05-18 — **Chrome auto-collapse — re-gated on viewport height, rAF dropped, verified end-to-end.** Corrects the entry above, which shipped unverified — on a phone the headers still didn't collapse. The collapse-on-scroll was gated on `(pointer: coarse)` and `requestAnimationFrame`-throttled; neither is exercisable in the dev preview (no coarse-pointer emulation; rAF is paused in a backgrounded tab — the same reason `_wtWaitFor` avoids it), so the scroll trigger had never actually been run. Two corrections, both also making it testable: (1) the gate moved from `(pointer: coarse)` to `matchMedia('(max-height: 540px)')` — the real problem is a *short* viewport (a landscape phone is ≤~450px tall; portrait phones are ≥568px and desktops far taller), so height is the correct signal and, unlike pointer type, is reliable and emulable; (2) the rAF throttle was dropped — the `scroll` handler now runs inline, since the browser already coalesces scroll events to one per frame and the handler's work (a `WeakMap` read, a compare, an occasional `classList.toggle`) is trivial. **Verification** (now possible): the capture-phase `document` scroll listener was first confirmed to receive element-scroll events — a synthetic `scroll` dispatched on `.main-scroll` is caught at `document` in the capture phase (programmatic `scrollTop` changes, by contrast, fire no `scroll` event in this preview, which had masked the pipeline). Then end-to-end at 844×390: a simulated content-pane scroll-down (`scrollTop` set + `scroll` dispatched) adds `body.chrome-collapsed`, a scroll-up removes it, a second scroll-down re-adds it; at 1280×900 the `max-height` gate is `false` and the same simulated scroll leaves the chrome shown. `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-05-18 — **Chrome auto-collapse — collapse the top header, not the nav-tab bar.** Per the user's clarification ("hide the top bar and the demo bar, keep the tab bar"), the collapse set changed: `body.chrome-collapsed` now collapses the `<header>` (56px) + `#demo-banner`, and `.nav-tabs-wrap` is left in place so section navigation stays reachable while the user is scrolled into content. Reclaims ~90px (header 56 + demo banner ~36) rather than ~80px. **Verification**: dev preview at 844×390 — toggling `body.chrome-collapsed` collapses `header` 56→0 and `#demo-banner` 36→0 while `.nav-tabs-wrap` holds at 45px and `.app-body` grows accordingly; `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-05-18 — **Guided tour — skipped on touch devices; mobile-tour scaffolding removed.** Per the user, adapting the spotlight tour for mobile wasn't worth it — the tour is now desktop-only and simply not shown on phones/tablets (the "Best viewed on a computer" notice already steers them to a desktop). **Skip**: `_wtStart()` (`src/walkthrough.js`) early-returns when `typeof window._pcIsTouchDevice === 'function' && window._pcIsTouchDevice()` — so the full tour never runs on a touch device, whether via the `_wtMaybeAutoStart` auto-start or a Help re-trigger. Gating `_wtStart` itself (not just the auto-start) means there is no path to the tour on mobile, so the now-unhandled tour can't be reached. The standalone Pro CTA (`_wtStartCta`, e.g. the account dropdown's "Upgrade to Pro") is unaffected — it is a centred scrollable modal that works on any viewport. **Removed** (now-dead mobile-tour code from the superseded "mobile landscape support" work): `_wtIsPortraitBlocked()`, `_wtDrawRotatePrompt()` and its `.wt-rotate-icon` CSS, the `_wtRender` portrait branch, the tap-to-navigate block in `_wtOverlayClick`, the `orientationchange` listeners in `_wtRunStart`/`_wtStartCta`/`_wtClose` (back to `resize`-only), and the device-aware welcome-copy split in `_wtCenterPreviewHTML` (the welcome step's keyboard hint is inline again). **Kept**: the `.wt-center` `max-height: calc(100dvh - 24px)` + `overflow: hidden auto` modal fix — the Pro CTA can still appear on a short viewport and benefits from it. **Mobile notice** (`src/mobile-notice.js`): dropped the "— rotate to landscape for the best mobile view" clause; it now ends "You can still use it with limited functionality on a phone or tablet." **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview — on desktop the tour still auto-runs and the welcome step shows the restored inline "use the arrow keys" copy; with `window._pcIsTouchDevice` stubbed to return `true`, `_wtStart({force:true})` creates no overlay and leaves `_wtActive` false; the mobile notice renders with no "landscape"/"rotate" text.
- 2026-05-19 — **Paid-ads tracking foundation — first-touch UTM attribution + Meta Pixel + Google Ads + GA4, all env-gated.** Laid before any paid-ads spend so signups carry permanent ad-campaign attribution. **(1) Attribution capture** (`src/main.js`): on every page load, if `utm_source`/`utm_medium`/`utm_campaign`/`gclid`/`fbclid` are in the URL, snapshot the params + `document.referrer` + `location.pathname+search` + `first_seen_at` into `localStorage.pc_attribution`. **First-touch wins** (industry-standard for SaaS — the campaign that first introduced a user gets credit, not whatever last-touched them before signup), so the block early-returns if a row already exists. Wrapped in `try/catch` for private-mode browsers where localStorage throws. `window._getAttribution()` reads the blob, returning `{}` for organic. **(2) Pixel inits** (`src/main.js`): three independent env gates — `VITE_GA4_ID` (G-XXXXXXXXXX) and `VITE_GOOGLE_ADS_ID` (AW-XXXXXXXXX) share a single gtag.js load (the script tag is created only when either is set; `gtag('config', ...)` runs per-ID), and `VITE_META_PIXEL_ID` separately loads fbevents.js + fires a `PageView`. With no env vars set, neither script loads and `window.gtag`/`window.fbq` stay undefined; the analytics.js helpers below feature-detect those globals and no-op. The Google Ads conversion `send_to` string (`AW-XXX/LABEL`, generated in the Google Ads dashboard) lives in a separate `VITE_GOOGLE_ADS_CONVERSION_SEND_TO` env var so the conversion action can be configured (or rotated) without touching the account ID; main.js exposes it to classic scripts as `window._GADS_CONV`. **(3) Signup wiring** (`src/app.js`): `authSubmit()`'s signup branch reads `window._getAttribution()` and passes the blob into `_sb.auth.signUp({ options: { data: { marketing_opt_in, attribution } } })`, so it lands in `auth.users.raw_user_meta_data.attribution` permanently. Queryable later via `select raw_user_meta_data->'attribution' from auth.users`. On success, calls new `_trackSignupConversion()` in analytics.js which fires Meta Pixel `CompleteRegistration`, GA4 `sign_up` (method:'email'), and Google Ads `conversion` with the `send_to` from `window._GADS_CONV`. The conversion event fires on signup form success — **not on email confirm** — because Google/Meta attribution chains rely on the ad-click → form-submit referrer chain, which the email-confirm redirect breaks. **(4) Person enrichment** (`src/analytics.js`): `_identifyUser()` now lifts `session.user.user_metadata.attribution` into PostHog person properties as `initial_utm_source`/`initial_utm_medium`/etc., so funnel reports can break down by ad campaign without a backend join. **(5) No migration** — `auth.users.raw_user_meta_data` is a JSONB column already; a SQL view to flatten it can be added later once campaigns produce data worth querying. **(6) Types** (`src/globals.d.ts`): declared `Window.gtag?`/`fbq?`/`dataLayer?`/`_fbq?`/`_getAttribution?`/`_GADS_CONV?` plus the `_track`/`_identifyUser`/`_resetAnalytics`/`_trackSignupConversion` function globals so strict-mode typecheck stays clean. **(7) `.env.example`** documents all four new vars with where to find each ID and what each enables. **Decision: first-touch over last-touch** — locked this session. Last-touch would attribute to whatever organic or direct source the user happened to arrive from on their final visit before signing up, which would undercount paid-ads credit and make campaign optimisation impossible. First-touch matches how Google Ads / Meta Ads Manager think about conversions, so cross-platform reports line up. **Decision: store in `auth.users.user_metadata` JSON, no dedicated table** — chosen for shipping speed; a `signup_attribution` table would require a migration, RLS policies, and an extra row write at signup. JSON works for any query we need short-term; if we ever want per-campaign joins from the app, a SQL view over `raw_user_meta_data->'attribution'` is a 10-minute add. **Pending user actions**: create the GA4 property, Google Ads account + conversion action, and Meta Pixel (via Meta Events Manager); fill the four `VITE_*` env vars into Cloudflare Pages env vars; verify the Pixel via Meta's Test Events tool after the first prod signup. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; with no env vars set, page load produces zero network calls to `googletagmanager.com` or `facebook.net`, `window.gtag`/`window.fbq` stay undefined, `_trackSignupConversion` no-ops without throwing. Live pixel verification deferred — needs the user's real GA4/Ads/Pixel IDs.
- 2026-05-19 — **Quote Builder gate — My Rates tab now reachable without an open quote.** The `#cb-sidebar-builder` Builder / My Rates tab bar (`#cb-tabs-wrap`) was hidden by `_cbRenderContext` whenever no quote/client was open, so rates could only be edited from inside a quote — unlike the Cabinet Library sidebar, whose equivalent tab bar is always shown. The gated empty state now shows the tab bar. **Mechanics**: the rates panel (`#cab-view-rates`) is nested inside `#cb-sidebar` while the gate empty-state lives in the sibling `#cb-context`, so a single display toggle can't pick which is "active". Added a `cbActiveTab` state global (`'builder'|'rates'`, in `cabinet-render.js` next to `cbMainView`); `switchCabTab` now sets it and, when gated (`!_cbCurrentClientId && !cbEditingQuoteId && !(cbEditingLibraryIdx>=0)`), toggles `#cb-context` (gate) against `#cb-sidebar` (rates) — the Builder tab restores the gate, My Rates reveals the rates panel. `_cbRenderContext` resets `#cb-context` display at the top of every call (the gated rates tab hides it) and syncs the tab per branch: the gate branch calls `switchCabTab(cbActiveTab)` (so a rate edit's `renderCBPanel` re-render doesn't kick you off My Rates), the library-edit branch forces `switchCabTab('builder')` (fixes a latent bug where a stale rates panel could stack over the template editor). In-project behaviour is unchanged. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview — on the gate the tab bar shows, My Rates renders the rates panel and hides the quote picker, Builder restores the picker, editing a rate stays on My Rates, and gate↔in-project↔exit transitions all render the correct header/editor/rates; no new console errors.
- 2026-05-21 — **Bugfix: `editQuoteInCB` / `editOrderInCB` now populate `_cbCurrentClientId` + `_cbCurrentClientName`.** Both functions wrote the project name into the `#cb-client` DOM input and `localStorage.pc_cq_client_name` but skipped the module-scope `_cbCurrentClientName` binding (`src/cabinet.js:155`, initial `''`). - 2026-05-22 — **Onboarding tour trimmed — removed the 8 per-section "X tab" intro steps.** Per the user ("the tour is too long, cut some steps — remove the tab steps"), dropped the dedicated nav-tab spotlight step that opened each section in `_wtSteps` (`src/walkthrough.js`): Clients tab / Quotes tab / Orders tab / Stock tab / Cabinet tab / Cut List tab / Schedule tab / Dashboard. **Kept** (per the clarifying questions): the early "Navigate between sections" overview step (step 1, spotlights `.nav-tabs`), and **all** export-related steps — Cut List's "Export & deduct stock" and Quote's "Send & convert" (user answered "none" when asked which export steps to cut). **Why it still works without the tab steps**: section navigation is driven by each step's `section` field, not by the tab step — when the first *remaining* step of a section renders, `_wtApplyContext` calls `switchSection` and `_wtGetPreClickTarget` animates the cursor to that section's nav tab, so the tab still lights up and the view still switches; the `cbView: 'results'` / `clView: 'library'` context that the removed Cabinet/Cut List tab steps carried is also present on the following step, so nothing is lost. No hardcoded step indices exist (`_wtLastIdx`/`findIndex`/relative `i±1` are all count-agnostic), so the cut needed no other edits. **Decision — `WT_VERSION` deliberately NOT bumped** (left at 3): the version gate exists to re-show the tour when there's something *new* worth seeing; removing steps shows returning users nothing new, so forcing a re-show isn't warranted. Bump only if the shortened tour should be re-displayed to people who already saw the long one. **Net**: tour 40 → 32 steps. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview (guest/demo) — `_wtStart()` opens the overlay, advancing 6× lands on "Client cards" (phase "Clients · Step 7 of 32") with the spotlight drawn and the Clients nav tab active; live `_wtSteps` confirms every section now starts on its content step and `anyTabTitle` is false; no console errors/warnings.
- 2026-05-22 — **Onboarding tour restructured into a tighter, uniform shape (follow-up to the trim above).** Per the user: two steps per nav tab, except Cabinet (four — one per sub-tab) and Cut List (three — sidebar + two sub-tabs); all top-toolbar steps moved to the end in right-to-left header order; `WT_VERSION` bumped 3→4 so users who completed the old tour are re-shown the new one once. **Final 26-step order**: Welcome, Navigate between sections, Clients (Client cards, Client profile), Quotes (Quote list, Quote editor), Orders (Order cards, Order detail), Stock (Material list, Adding materials), Cabinet (Quote Builder → Cabinet Builder → My Rates → Cabinet Library), Cut List (Sheets & pieces → Cut List Library → Cut Layout), Schedule (Order queue, Gantt calendar), Dashboard (Live overview, Quick actions), Toolbar (Account, Settings, Help, New features), Pro CTA. **Decisions**: (1) Quotes keeps Quote list + Quote editor and drops 'Send & convert' — that removes the last 'export' step the user had asked to keep the turn before, but the new 2-per-tab rule supersedes it; the Quote editor step gained `preClickCard: '.quote-card'` so it still opens a populated quote now that the card-opening 'Send & convert' step is gone. (2) Cut List drops the per-item Sheet stock / Piece list / Optimise / Visual layout / Export steps for one combined sidebar step ('Sheets & pieces', `clView: 'layout'`, target `.cl-left`) plus the two `.cl-right` sub-tabs (`#cl-tab-library`, `#cl-tab-layout`). (3) Cabinet's four steps spotlight the four sub-tab elements — `#cb-main-tab-results` (Quote Builder), `#cab-tab-builder` (Cabinet Builder), `#cab-tab-rates` (My Rates, via `subtab: 'rates'`), `#cb-main-tab-library` (Cabinet Library); a browser probe confirmed `switchCBMainView('results')` does NOT reset the active sidebar sub-tab, so the My Rates step shows its rates content. (4) Toolbar order is the visual header reversed (DOM/visual L→R is New features, Help, Settings, Account ⇒ R→L is Account, Settings, Help, New features), confirmed by measuring the four buttons' x-positions in the preview; phase relabelled 'Toolbar'; the Settings step title lost the now-misplaced word 'first'. **No hardcoded step indices** exist (`_wtLastIdx`/`findIndex`/relative nav are count-agnostic), so the re-order needed no other edits. **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview reloaded, a full keyboard drive-through rendered all 26 steps in order with a spotlight on each (Cabinet + Cut List sub-tabs included) and completed into the CTA; no console warnings (an unreachable/skipped step logs one) or errors; screenshot confirmed the live counter reads 'Step 7 of 26'.

- 2026-05-23 — **PostHog wired into the marketing landing page (build-time key injection).** The landing (`landing.html`, served at `/`) loads none of the app bundle and is copied verbatim into `dist/` by `copyLandingPlugin` (vite.config.mjs), so it can't read `import.meta.env` the way `src/main.js` does. Added the official PostHog browser snippet to `landing.html`'s `<head>` (placed *after* the auth/Stripe redirect so pass-through visitors don't fire a stray landing pageview) using `__VITE_POSTHOG_KEY__` / `__VITE_POSTHOG_HOST__` placeholders. `copyLandingPlugin` now reads the source, `split`/`join`-replaces both placeholders from `loadEnv(mode, cwd, 'VITE_')` (`.env.local` locally, `process.env` on Cloudflare), and writes `dist/index.html` + `dist/landing.html` (previously a verbatim `copyFileSync`). A guard (`if (!k || k.charAt(0)==='_') return;`) makes the snippet a no-op in dev — the plugin only runs at build, so in dev the placeholders survive and PostHog never inits, keeping dev traffic out of prod analytics (matches the existing `VITE_POSTHOG_KEY` philosophy). Same PostHog project + same origin as `/os`, so a visitor's anonymous landing activity stitches to their identified profile after signup. Init opts: `capture_pageview` + `autocapture` on (CTA clicks feed the conversion funnel), `disable_session_recording: true` to conserve the free-tier replay quota for in-app sessions (flip to record landing replays). Config converted to function form to read `mode`; placeholder is deliberately NOT `%VITE_%` so Vite's dev html-env transform can't half-replace it (only the build plugin does). **Verification**: `npm run typecheck` + `npm run build` clean; built `dist/index.html` has 0 leftover placeholders, the real `phc_…` key + EU host injected, `posthog.init` present, and `dist/os/index.html` (the app) untouched (0 inline `phc_`, still uses the bundled SDK). Dev preview via the raw-source "Landing" server: `window.posthog` undefined, no `array.js` injected, placeholder intact, 0 console errors. Isolated active-path test (throwaway file, fake token): snippet runs → `window.posthog` defined, `array.js` loaded from `eu-assets.i.posthog.com`, `init` wired, 0 console errors.
- 2026-05-23 — **Mobile-native responsive pass (7 phases, 7 commits).** Replaced the May-18 portrait horizontal-scroll hack (`styles.css` `min-width:840px` + body x-scroll) with a true single-column "one pane at a time" layout. **Core mechanism:** `body[data-mv]` ("list" | "editor") + a two-class marker contract (`.mv-pane-editor` on each section's sidebar/editor, `.mv-pane-list` on its main/list pane) added to `index.html`, so one `@media (max-width:760px)` block stacks every heterogeneous panel (`.sidebar`/`.main-content`, `.cl-left`/`.cl-right`, inline-width Cabinet/Schedule sidebars) uniformly and shows one pane at a time — chosen over pure-CSS because the drill-in needs JS state. New `src/mobile-nav.js` exposes `_mvSet`/`_mvIsMobile` (matchMedia ≤760px)/`_mvShowEditor`/`_mvShowList` + injects a global sticky "← Back to list" bar; `data-mv` defaults to `list` synchronously to avoid a flash. Drill-in wired by appending one guarded line to the *existing* card→editor / back→list fns (`loadQuoteIntoSidebar`, `loadOrderIntoSidebar`, `editStockItem`/`_stockRevealForm`, `editClient`/`_clientsRevealForm`, `_clLoadCutlist`/`_clDoOpenLibraryCutlist`, `cbEditCabinetFromOutput`/`cbEditLibraryEntry`/`cbStartNewLibraryEntry`, the `_q*`/`_o*` new/exit/clear fns) plus a `switchSection` reset and a catch-all in `_renderProjectHeader`'s back button. Cabinet/Cut-List creation lives in the sidebar (hidden in list view), so `.mv-only` (`display:none` desktop, shown ≤760px) "+ Add" / "Open builder" buttons were added to those list panes for reachability. **Decisions:** (1) two breakpoints — `@media (max-width:760px)` for the single-column *layout*, `@media (pointer:coarse), (max-width:760px)` (OR) for *touch sizing* — the OR arm makes touch sizing render in a desktop preview window (pointer:fine) so it stays verifiable, and a narrow mouse window getting fat targets is harmless. (2) Phase 4 line-item cards are **pure CSS** — the stable column classes (`.col-qty` etc.) carry their labels via `::before`, so no markup/JS change and the `hide-hrs`/`hide-disc` toggles still work. (3) Phase 5 canvas pinch-zoom transforms the canvas via CSS (bitmap untouched → `toDataURL` PDF export unaffected); gated to phones/coarse so desktop hover/toolbar is unchanged; `touch-action` flips to `none` only while zoomed so the results list still scrolls at fit; toolbar re-renders replace the canvas (free reset). (4) Phase 6 schedule agenda is a `_mvIsMobile()` render-branch reusing the sidebar's existing `sortedEvents`, with sort/filter/hours relocated into the agenda header and the redundant sidebar hidden. **Bugs fixed in polish:** `input[type="tel"]` was missing from the base field rule (phone field rendered browser-default narrow); `.oc-info` lacked `min-width:0` (long quote/order card titles pushed the value off-screen). Mobile notice (`_pcMaybeShowMobileNotice`) reframed from the desktop-first "Best viewed on a computer" warning to a positive once-per-session "Optimised for mobile" welcome (tap-to-open / Back / pinch-zoom tips); kept the `_pcIsTouchDevice` gate + the `_wtMaybeAutoStart` call (tour still skips touch). **Gotchas confirmed:** chrome-collapse is `max-height:540px` (landscape) so it never fights the portrait layout; resize-handle is `display:none` on mobile so its inline-width persistence can't leak; `optimize()` now also `_mvShowList()`s so the freshly-rendered cut layout (in the list pane) is visible. Verified at 360/390px across all 8 sections + desktop regression at 1440px (two-pane, table, 7-col grid all intact); `npm run typecheck` + `npm run build` clean. Deferred: cut-list `.cl-table` inline inputs stay sub-16px (iOS may zoom); agenda "Sort: Manual" has no drag-reorder.
- 2026-05-23 — **Paid-ads tracking — landing-page coverage fix (the May-19 attribution foundation only fired on `/os`).** The first-touch attribution capture + GA4 + Google Ads + Meta Pixel from the 2026-05-19 work all live in `src/main.js`, which only loads on the app at `/os`. But the marketing landing page (`landing.html`) is the home page at `/` — where every paid-ad click actually lands — and it loads PostHog only, not `main.js`. Its CTAs are bare `href="/os"` that drop the query string. **Net:** an ad click arriving at `/?gclid=…&utm_source=…` never had its params captured (the snapshot code wasn't on the page), and the `_gcl_aw`/`_fbc` first-party cookies were never set, so by the time `main.js` ran on `/os` (params now stripped) every paid signup looked organic — Google Ads/Meta couldn't attribute conversions and smart bidding was blind. A regression from when the landing page was split out to `/` (the attribution code predates the split, when the app was at root). **Fix (3 edits, no schema):** (1) `landing.html` — added an inline tracking block after the PostHog snippet (placed after the auth/Stripe redirect so pass-through visitors don't fire stray events) that mirrors `main.js` exactly: same `pc_attribution` localStorage snapshot (first-touch, never overwrite once set), the GA4 + Google Ads gtag.js loader, and the Meta Pixel init + PageView. (2) `vite.config.mjs` `copyLandingPlugin` — extended the build-time placeholder injection (already used for PostHog) to swap `__VITE_GA4_ID__` / `__VITE_GOOGLE_ADS_ID__` / `__VITE_META_PIXEL_ID__` from the build env; `landing.html` is copied verbatim so `import.meta.env` isn't available inside it. (3) `landing.js` — forwards the marketing params (utm_*/gclid/fbclid) onto every `a[href^="/os"]` so the app page sees them directly too. **Why this fully fixes it:** the pixels set `_gcl_aw`/`_fbc` and the snapshot writes `pc_attribution` on `/`, all same-origin, so `/os` reads them at signup; the param-forwarding is belt-and-braces. **Decisions:** (1) duplicate the tracking inline in `landing.html` rather than share a module — the landing is copied verbatim and loads none of the app bundle by design; both copies carry `mirrors src/main.js` comments to stay in sync. (2) only the three pixel IDs are injected on the landing — the Google Ads conversion `send_to` is not, because the conversion event fires at `/os` signup, not on the landing. (3) consent-mode / GDPR banner not added here (matches existing `main.js` behaviour; deferred as a separate effort). **Env-gated identically to main.js:** with no IDs set the injected value is `''`, the inline `val()` guard returns `''`, and every block no-ops — zero network calls. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean; a build with dummy IDs injects all three into `dist/index.html` (the home page) with zero leftover `__VITE_*__` placeholders; a clean build renders `val('')` ×3 (no-op) with the attribution snapshot + block structure intact. **Still pending (user-side):** create the GA4 / Google Ads / Meta accounts and set the four `VITE_*` vars in Cloudflare Pages (GA4 ID `G-HXN3J8V1YX` captured this session), then verify pixels live after the first prod signup.
