- 2026-05-23 — **Demo writes nudge instead of walling (guest UX).** A logged-out demo visitor who tried to save/add anything got the full-screen sign-in wall (`_requireAuth` → `_showAuth`), and the 6 create flows that reach `_enforceFreeLimit` without a `_requireAuth` guard first (`resolveClient`, `_loadCBClientById`, `cbStartNewLibraryEntry`, `cbDuplicateLibraryEntry`, `_clDuplicateLibraryCutlist`, `_clDuplicateCutlist`) got the Stripe "Upgrade to Pro" modal — both jarring for someone just exploring (the demo seeds every library at the 5-item cap, so a guest is *always* at the limit). Now all three chokepoints route to a new debounced **`_demoNudge()`** (`src/demo.js`): an `info`-style toast "You're exploring the demo — sign in to save your work." that leaves them exactly where they are. **Wiring:** `_requireAuth` (app.js) — `if (window._demoMode) { _demoNudge(); return false; }` before `_showAuth()`; `_enforceFreeLimit` (limits.js) — guest branch `if (window._demoMode && !_userId)` skips the upgrade modal *and* the `free_tier_limit_hit` analytics event (a seeded-cap hit isn't a real limit signal); `_demoBlockWrite` (demo.js) — the `_db()`-level backstop now calls `_demoNudge()` instead of `_requireAuth()`, so unguarded fire-and-forget inline edits (e.g. `updateClient`) nudge too. **Decisions:** (1) **guest-only** — `_demoNudge` early-returns when `_userId` is set, so a signed-in user mid-walkthrough (also `_demoMode === true`) sees zero behaviour change (telling them to "sign in" would be nonsense). (2) **debounced 4000ms** (> the 3500ms toast lifetime) so rapid inline edits / sliders can't spam the toast stack. (3) explicit sign-in entry points (demo banner, account menu, pricing deep-link, walkthrough CTA) still call `_showAuth()` directly — the user can always *choose* to sign in; we just don't *force* it on a blocked write. (4) signed-in free user at cap still gets the upgrade modal unchanged (monetization path intact). **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview (signed-in session) — source-inspected the live bundle to confirm all three demo branches present; `_demoBlockWrite({_isSingle:true})` returns the benign `{data:null, error:{_demo:true,…}}` shape; two back-to-back backstop calls produced exactly **one** `toast info` with the right copy (debounce works); after adding the guest-only guard, the same call while signed in produced **zero** toasts.
- 2026-05-23 — **Unified list/library filter bars (Cabinet Library as the reference).** The search/filter input + Import/Export buttons differed in shape, height, and layout across every list tab (Clients/Quotes/Orders/Stock/Cut List Library) — Quotes/Orders crammed search + status tabs + sort `<select>` + Import/Export onto one wrapping line; inputs were pill-shaped 20px-radius `.order-search-input` (5px 10px) in some tabs vs rounded-rect inline-styled in others. Standardised on the Cabinet Library layout via four shared classes in `styles.css` (`.lib-filter-row` / `input.lib-filter-input` / `.lib-filter-btn` / `.lib-toggle-row`) + `.lib-sort-select`: **row 1** is the search/filter input (`flex:1`, 13px, 8px 12px pad, `var(--radius)` 10px, `surface2`) followed by `↓ Export` / `↑ Import` (and Stock's count + `PDF`) all the same height on one line; **row 2** (`.lib-toggle-row`) carries any toggles — status pills (`.ofilter-tab`) + the sort dropdown — moved off the search line per the user ask. `cabinet-render.js` (the reference) and `cutlist.js` converted to the classes (visually identical); `quotes.js`/`orders.js` split into the two rows; `clients.js` search-row reclassed + its sort moved to a toggle row; `stock.js` search-row reclassed (its category pills already were a separate line). **Two gotchas:** (a) the input class needs an `input.` prefix — the global `input[type="text"]` rule (`styles.css:701`, specificity 0,1,1) otherwise out-specifies a bare `.lib-filter-input` (0,1,0) and forced text-type inputs to 7px-10px pad / 7px radius while search-type inputs got the class values, *recreating* the inconsistency; `input.lib-filter-input` ties at 0,1,1 and wins on source order. (b) the same global rule sets `select{width:100%}`, which (combined with the inline `margin-left:auto`) made the sort `<select>` blow out to full width and wrap to its own line — `.lib-sort-select { width:auto; flex:0 0 auto }` (class 0,1,0 beats bare `select` 0,0,1) fixes it. Retired `.order-search-input` / `.order-filter-tabs` (now unused; kept `.ofilter-tab`); updated the print-hide rule and the `/`-focus selector in `auth.js` to the new class. Removed the old per-tab inline styles. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview at 1600px — Orders/Stock/Clients/Cut-List bars screenshotted (search+Import/Export one line, toggles below); computed styles confirmed identical across text-type (Clients/Cut List) and search-type (Orders/Stock) inputs (33px tall, 8px 12px pad, 10px radius, 13px font); 0 console errors. Quotes/Cabinet Library bars are empty-state in the demo data but use the same templates as Orders/the reference.
- 2026-05-23 — **Cache-busting for the classic `/src/*.js` scripts (stale-deploy fix).** User reported the live app showing an old version in a normal Safari window but the current build in a Private window, with a "hard refresh" not helping. Root cause: the 34 classic `<script defer src="/src/*.js">` tags (which hold ~all app logic) keep stable filenames across deploys, and Cloudflare Pages' default browser cache (`Cache-Control: public, max-age=14400, must-revalidate` — confirmed via `curl -I https://procabinet.app/src/cutlist.js`) let the browser reuse them for 4h without revalidating. Only the Vite-hashed `/assets/index-*.js` bundle (the `main.js` bridge) busts on deploy; the carved domain files don't. **No service worker involved** — verified absent in source, git history, and at the origin (probed `/sw.js` etc., all return Cloudflare's catch-all HTML). The misleading clue was "hard refresh doesn't fix it": the user pressed Cmd+Shift+R, which is Chrome's shortcut and a no-op in Safari (whose reload-from-origin is Cmd+Opt+R), so the cache was never actually bypassed; Private windows worked because they start with an empty cache. **Fix in `vite.config.mjs`:** (1) `versionClassicScriptsPlugin` (runs after `copyLandingPlugin`, once the app HTML is at `dist/os/index.html`) sha256-hashes each `dist/src/*.js` and appends `?v=<8hex>` to its `<script src>` so the URL changes whenever the file changes. (2) New root `_headers` file copied to `dist/_headers` by `copyHeadersPlugin`: `/assets/*` and `/src/*` → `max-age=31536000, immutable` (safe now that both URL kinds change on content change), and `/`, `/os`, `/os/` → `max-age=0, must-revalidate` (the lynchpin — HTML always revalidates so the browser always reads the latest `?v=` URLs). Self-healing on the next load after deploy (HTML was already must-revalidate, so no Cloudflare purge needed); old `/src/*.js` cache entries are simply orphaned by the new query string. **Verification:** `npm run build` clean; `dist/_headers` present; all 34 `/src` tags carry distinct `?v=` hashes (grep: stamped 34 / total 34 / unstamped 0). Deployed to production (GitHub Actions run 26345856691, green in 49s) and verified live — `/os` serves the stamped `?v=` URLs, `/src/*` returns `max-age=31536000, immutable` (was `max-age=14400`), and `/os` HTML stays `max-age=0, must-revalidate`. Landing-page `/landing.js` + `/landing.css` are still unhashed at root (same latent 4h-cache bug, lower stakes) — left as an optional follow-up.
- 2026-05-23 — **Cache-busting follow-ups: landing assets + CI Node 24.** Two follow-ups to the `/src` cache fix above. (1) **Landing page**: `versionClassicScriptsPlugin` now also stamps the unhashed root assets `/landing.js` + `/landing.css` (the only refs the marketing home carried without a hash) with `?v=<contenthash>` in both `dist/index.html` and the `dist/landing.html` back-compat alias; `_headers` gains `immutable` rules for both plus a `must-revalidate` rule for `/landing.html`. Closes the same latent 4h-stale-cache bug on the landing page that the previous entry flagged. (2) **CI Node 24**: bumped the deprecated GitHub Actions to Node-24-native majors — `actions/checkout` v4→v6, `actions/setup-node` v4→v6, `cloudflare/wrangler-action` v3→v4 (verified v4's `action.yml` is `using: node24` and keeps the `apiToken`/`accountId`/`command` inputs). With all three now native Node 24, the `FORCE_JAVASCRIPT_ACTIONS_TO_NODE24` workaround env var in `deploy.yml` is redundant and was removed. **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` + `npm run build` clean; both landing HTML files carry stamped `?v=` URLs (0 unstamped), app `/src` still 34/34, `dist/_headers` has the landing rules.
- 2026-05-24 — **Landing-page PostHog: session recording turned ON (follow-up to the wiring above).** User reported landing-page visits never appear in PostHog session replays. Root cause: the original snippet set `disable_session_recording: true` (a deliberate quota-saving choice), so the landing page captured `$pageview`/autocapture events but was never recorded — and replays of signups began at `/os` with the landing entry missing. Flipped to `disable_session_recording: false` in `landing.html`. Because the landing (`/`) and app (`/os`) share one PostHog project + origin, a visitor's replay is now one continuous session spanning landing → app. Quota note: replays count toward the free-tier 5k/mo; add a `session_recording: { sampleRate: '0.5' }` block to sample if landing traffic grows. **Events side was already fine** (the "not picking up" complaint was specifically about replays, not events): served the production `dist/` build via `vite preview` and watched real traffic — all SDK assets 200 incl. `/array/<token>/config.js` (proves the key is valid for EU), project remote-config permissive (`autocapture_opt_out:false`), and a real `$pageview` POST to `eu.i.posthog.com/i/v0/e/` → 200. The automatic initial `$pageview` only fired after forcing `document.visibilityState='visible'`: posthog-js defers the first pageview until the tab is visible and the preview browser renders hidden — a test-harness artifact, not a production bug. **Verification of the recording fix**: rebuilt (`disable_session_recording: false` present in `dist/index.html`); in the preview `posthog.sessionRecordingStarted()` → true, `posthog-recorder.js` loaded (200 — it is NOT fetched when recording is disabled), and `get_session_replay_url()` returns a valid replay link. `npm run build` clean.
- 2026-05-24 — **PDF outputs — spacing/layout cleanup pass** (all 5 jsPDF builders in `src/cutlist.js`). Added an offline QA harness `scripts/render-pdf-samples.mjs` that loads the real PDF-drawing slice from `cutlist.js` into a Node `vm` sandbox (stubbed app globals + seed data) and writes one sample per template to `pdf-samples/` (gitignored) — lets the builders be reviewed/diffed without clicking through the app. Fixes found and applied: **(1) garbled minus sign** — the Discount totals row used U+2212 (not in jsPDF's WinAnsi Helvetica), which rendered as `"` with broken letter-spacing; switched to ASCII `-` in `_buildQuotePDF` + `_buildOrderDocPDF`. **(2) logo-header collision** — `_drawBizHeader` returns the height it consumes but every caller hard-advanced `y` by a fixed amount sized for the *no-logo* header, so a logo's name/address/ABN caption overprinted the divider + client row; all callers now do `y += Math.max(<fixed>, hdrH)` and the cut-list `pageHeader()` returns its divider Y so summary content flows below it (no-logo output unchanged — `Math.max` floors to the old constant). **(3) stock table column collisions** — fixed-x columns were too cramped (Size ran into Supplier, Material/Supplier truncated mid-word); rebuilt with proper geometry, width-aware ellipsis truncation (`fit()` via `getTextWidth`), right-aligned Qty/Alert/Value, and a `—` fallback for hardware with no dimensions. **(4) quote total tie-out** — total box used `fmt0` (rounded to whole pounds) while the breakdown showed pence; switched to `fmt` (2dp) so it matches the line items and the order-doc totals; removed now-unused `fmt0`. **Polish:** added `_pdfNiceDate()` so due dates render "15 July 2026" (was raw ISO `2026-07-15`) on the work order + order docs; stripped a doubled full stop in the quote acceptance line for businesses ending in "Co.". `npm run typecheck` clean; all 10 samples re-rendered + visually verified.
- 2026-05-25 — **DXF / CNC export of the nested cut layout** (`src/cutlist.js`, new `exportLayoutDXF` + `_buildLayoutDXF`/`_dxfSheetBlock`/`_dxfRect`/`_dxfText`/`_dxfTextLeft`/`_dxfNum`/`_dxfFilenameSafe`; `DXF` button in `#layout-toolbar-top` beside PDF). Exports the optimiser's nested layout as **one** DXF for import into CAM / CNC nesting software — every unique sheet packing (`results.uniqueLayouts`) tiled left-to-right into a single drawing, each block translated by a running X offset (gap 100 mm / 4 in) and topped with an identifying caption (`Sheet i/N: <name> [WxH] xQty`). `$EXTMAX` spans the full tiled extent. **Decisions:** (1) **DXF, not G-code** — G-code is machine-specific (post-processor, tool dia, feeds/speeds, controller dialect); the correct handoff is a DXF the user drops into their own CAM, which posts for their machine. (2) **R12 (`AC1009`) + old-style closed `POLYLINE`** for maximum CAM compatibility (Vectric/Fusion/AlphaCAM/Cabinet Vision); LWPOLYLINE needs R14+ and some minimal readers reject it. (3) **Origin flip** — the packer uses a top-left/y-down canvas origin; DXF + CNC beds are bottom-left/y-up, so every y maps through `sheetH - y` (skip it and every part mirrors vertically). (4) **Cut size, not finished** — draws `placed.w/h` (edge-band trim already subtracted by `_trimmedDims` in `optimize`), i.e. what the machine actually cuts. (5) **Pro-gated** via `_enforceProFeature()` — a data export, mirroring the CSV gating (PDF stays free). (6) **One combined file** (`<name>-nested.dxf`) — chosen over one-file-per-sheet (the original cut), so a single click → single download, no zip dep and no browser multi-download prompt. Geometry on a `PARTS` layer, sheet outline on `SHEET`, labels (part name + cut dims, ASCII-only, unit-aware text height) + sheet captions on `LABELS`; `$INSUNITS` = 4 (mm) / 1 (inch) from `window.units`. **Verification** (dev preview, demo mode): `_buildLayoutDXF` over a synthetic 2-sheet (2440×1220 + 3050×1300) layout — asserted single HEADER/ENTITIES/EOF, polyline/seqend counts, tiling offset (sheet 2 outline at x=2540 = 2440+100; its part at x=2540, y=1300−500=800), `$EXTMAX` 5590×1370, both captions; per-sheet y-flip (1220−720=500, 1220−300=920) + imperial branch (`$INSUNITS` 1, 48−30=18) from the earlier per-sheet build; real `optimize()` → `exportLayoutDXF()` → single `Westside-12B-Cut-List-nested.dxf`, "Exported nested DXF (3 sheets)", zero console errors. `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-05-25 — **Cut type toggle: panel saw (guillotine) vs CNC router (nested)** (`src/cutlist.js` `cutMethod` state + `packSheetNested`/`_pruneFreeRects` + `setCutMethod`/`_syncCutMethodToggle`; `optimize()` picks the packer; toggle in `#cl-action-bar` in `index.html`; `.cut-method*` styles in `styles.css`; init sync in `src/app.js`). The optimiser was guillotine-only (`packSheetRecGuillotine`, edge-to-edge cuts for a panel saw). Added a second non-guillotine packer for CNC routers, where the tool follows each part outline so parts can be placed freely and packed denser. **Decisions:** (1) **MaxRects (Best-Short-Side-Fit)** for the nested packer — free placement, good rectangle density, ~120 lines, no deps. (2) **Gap = the existing per-sheet kerf** (user choice) — in router mode the kerf value is the bit-diameter clearance; no new field. Implemented by inflating the bin by `gap` and every part's footprint by `gap` (place real `w×h` at the footprint origin), which guarantees ≥`gap` between neighbours while parts can still reach the real sheet edge. (3) **Identical output shape** — `packSheetNested` returns `{ placed:[{x,y,w,h,item,rotated}], leftover }` exactly like the guillotine packer, so the layout viewer, stats, PDF and DXF export all consume it unchanged. Grain constraints reuse the same `orientOf` rule. Default stays guillotine; choice persists to `localStorage.pc_cut_method`; switching re-runs `optimize()` when a layout is on screen. A `/** @type {{placed:any[],leftover:any[]}} */` annotation on the ternary result avoids a TS7022 circular-inference error from unioning the two packer return types. **Verification** (dev preview): direct packer test on a 28-part pool — nested gave 0 overlaps, 0 out-of-bounds, 0 gap violations and higher utilisation (91.4% vs guillotine 87.9% on sheet 1); end-to-end toggle flips `localStorage` + active button + re-optimises; real layouts rendered at 94% (nested) vs 92% (guillotine) with the expected free-vs-edge-to-edge structure. `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-05-30 — **QuickBooks Online + Xero invoice integration — one-way push (code complete, DB live, 4 edge functions deployed).** Adds the ability to turn an order into a **draft** invoice in the user's connected QuickBooks/Xero account from the order card. Pro-only. Full plan: `~/.claude/plans/splendid-gliding-flute.md`. **Locked decisions (confirmed with the user up front):** (1) **one-way push only** — app → accounting; pulling paid/unpaid status back is out of scope (future). (2) **both providers** ship together — the OAuth scaffold, token store, push flow and UI are provider-agnostic, with QBO-vs-Xero specifics isolated to `supabase/functions/_shared/providers.ts`. (3) **draft** invoices (Xero `Status:"DRAFT"`; QBO created-but-not-emailed) so the user reviews before sending. (4) **OAuth tokens encrypted at rest** (AES-GCM, key `ACCOUNTING_TOKEN_KEY` in Supabase secrets) — refresh tokens grant ongoing access to a financial system. **Schema** (migration `accounting_integration`, applied via MCP; SCHEMA.md § 3.21/3.22): `accounting_connections` (one row per user+provider; `access_token_enc`/`refresh_token_enc` + `expires_at`/`realm_id`/`tenant_id`/`org_name`/`default_tax_code`/`status`) and `accounting_invoice_links` (order ↔ external invoice for the "Synced" chip + deep link + re-push dedupe). **Token columns are hidden from the client by column-level grants** — `revoke all … from authenticated` then `grant select (safe cols only)`, so a client `select=*` is denied at the column level (verified live: `permission denied` on `*`/`refresh_token_enc`, success on the safe projection); RLS is SELECT-only (owner), writes go via the service role in the functions (mirrors `subscriptions` § 3.17). **Edge functions** (Deno; shared `_shared/{cors,auth,crypto,providers,connection}.ts`): `accounting-oauth-start` (verify_jwt true → signed-`state` authorize URL), `accounting-oauth-callback` (**verify_jwt false** — provider redirect, secured by HMAC `state` + one-time code; exchanges code→tokens, captures Xero tenant / QBO realm, picks a default tax code, encrypted upsert, 302 → `/os?accounting=connected`), `accounting-push-invoice` (verify_jwt true), `accounting-disconnect` (verify_jwt true; provider revoke + row delete). Token refresh in `connection.ts` re-encrypts + **persists the rotated refresh token** (mandatory for Xero, which rotates every refresh). **Two design deviations worth recording:** (a) **invoice line amounts are computed client-side** (`_accountingBuildLines` in `src/accounting.js`) and passed in the push body — because cabinet costing (`calcCBLine`) lives in the frontend and the figures must match the Invoice PDF exactly. This is safe: it's the user's own data going into their own accounting system as a reviewable draft; the function still re-checks order ownership server-side and sources the customer/contact from the DB (never the body). (b) **Tax**: the app carries a single order-level `tax %` but QB/Xero compute tax from their own configured rate codes, so on push every line is tax-exclusive and gets the connection's auto-picked `default_tax_code` (or the provider no-tax code when order tax = 0); order-level markup/stock-markup are pushed as their own lines and the order discount as a pre-tax negative line. Line items + markup tie out to the cent; the grand total matches when the chosen provider rate equals the order's tax %. The QBO `ItemRef`/Xero `AccountCode` requirements are satisfied by resolving a default Service item / REVENUE account per push — the area most likely to need a tweak during live sandbox testing. **Frontend** (`src/accounting.js` + account-dropdown entry, order-card "Sync ▾" button + "Synced ✓" chip, `?accounting=` return handler, boot hydrate, Pro gate via `_enforceProFeature`). **Verification:** `npm run typecheck` clean; `get_advisors` clean (no new lints); 4 functions deployed ACTIVE; smoke tests green (oauth-start OPTIONS→204+CORS, unauth POST→401 on all JWT fns, callback no-params→302 `?accounting=error` confirming verify_jwt=false); column-grant token-hiding confirmed on the live DB; dev preview — Sync button renders on order cards, Pro gate fires for free users, connect popup (both provider cards) renders for Pro, missing-data handled with zero console errors. **Committed** `1b1eab9` (code; migration file staged). **Pending (credentials only):** register the Intuit + Xero developer apps (redirect URI `https://mhzneruvlfmhnsohfrdo.supabase.co/functions/v1/accounting-oauth-callback`) and set the 6 secrets (`QBO_CLIENT_ID/SECRET`, `QBO_ENVIRONMENT`, `XERO_CLIENT_ID/SECRET`, `ACCOUNTING_TOKEN_KEY`, `ACCOUNTING_STATE_SECRET`), then run the live sandbox connect → push → disconnect + token-refresh check. PLAN.md entry stays 🚧 until that live check passes.

- 2026-06-08 — **Base types: flat price → labour hours**. The My Rates "Base" section now stores `{name, refHours}` instead of `{name, price}`, matching the Carcass/Door/Drawer type lists. Base/plinth fabrication is now priced as labour (refHours × labour rate, flat — no power-law, since a plinth's effort doesn't scale with cabinet volume), not a fixed material add-on. **Calc** (`src/cabinet-calc.js`): removed `baseType.price` from `cabinetMat`/`matCost` in both `calcCBSections` and `calcCBLine`; added `baseHrs` to `cabinetLabour` and `autoLabour` respectively. Uses an **exact-match** lookup (`?.refHours || 0`) rather than `_typeRefHours` — base is optional, so an unset/unknown base must contribute 0 hours instead of falling back to the first list item. **UI** (`src/cabinet-render.js`): Base section switched from `listItems`(price/currency) to `typeListItems`(refHours/"hrs"); editor dropdown label shows `(Xhrs)` instead of `(+£price)`. **Defaults** (`src/cabinet.js`): None 0 / Plinth 0.3 / Feet·Legs 0.4 / Castors 0.3 / Frame 0.5. **Migration**: legacy `{name, price}` rows are converted on load — both the localStorage-init path (`src/cabinet.js`) and the DB-overlay path (`src/app.js` `_applyBizInfoFromDB`) drop `price` and default `refHours` to 0 (price≠hours, so no auto-conversion — users re-enter hours). `default_base_types` jsonb column unchanged (shape is `{name, ...}`, only the second key changed). Quote prices for cabinets with a base change as a result. Typecheck clean; verified Base section renders "hrs" in dev preview.
- 2026-06-08 — **Finishing stock items measured in litres + coverage rate that prices quotes by area.** Paint/oil/lacquer items (category `Finishing`) now carry a volume and a coverage figure instead of a generic unit count. **Decisions (confirmed with the user):** (1) quote behaviour = **price by surface area** — adding a finish to a quote/order creates a stock line with `unit_price = cost-per-litre ÷ coverage` (£/m², or £/ft² imperial) and `qty = area`, so the user types the surface area and the line computes the cost; (2) imperial unit = **US gallons + ft²/gal** (`L_PER_USGAL = 3.785411784`); (3) **canonical storage is metric** — `qty` = litres, `cost` = £/L, `coverage_sqm` = m²/L — and the stock form converts to gallons/ft²-per-gal only when `window.units !== 'metric'`. **Schema** (migration `stock_finishing_coverage`, applied to `mhzneruvlfmhnsohfrdo`): widened `stock_items.qty` from `integer`→`numeric` (litres need decimals) and added `coverage_sqm numeric`. **Implementation:** new `Finishing` branch in `stockCatChanged`/`addStockItem`/`saveStockEdit`/`_stockAutosaveRun`/`editStockItem` mirroring the existing Edge-Banding special-case; a coverage input (`stock-fin-coverage`) + relabelled Volume/Low/Cost fields (`_setLabel`); `_fin*` conversion helpers + `_finQuoteLine(stockItem)` (shared by `_qAddStockLineFromLibrary`/`_oAddStockLineFromLibrary` in app.js, returns null for non-finishing/zero-coverage so they fall back to per-unit cost); a decimal-aware inline qty editor `setStockQtyFin` (the generic `setStockQty` strips non-digits); stock rows show coverage in the Dimensions col + derived £/m² (or £/ft²) in the Thickness col, with the qty pill/section totals in L or gal. `duplicateStockItem` carries `coverage_sqm`. `database.types.ts` updated (added `coverage_sqm`). `npm run typecheck` clean. On `feat/quote-order-overhaul-mockups`; **not pushed**.
- 2026-06-08 — **Orders become first-class shareable live links (their own `share_token`, not the origin quote's).** Reverses the earlier "order reuses the origin quote's `/q` link" decision (2026-06-05/06 entries) — an order with no shared quote could never produce a link, and the sample has 1 quote vs 4 orders. **Decision (confirmed):** the customer page now serves the order's **own** line items; `quote-public-get` resolves the token against `quotes` first, then `orders`, returning the identical response shape plus a `kind:'quote'|'order'` flag; `quote-messages` likewise resolves either and tags the customer insert with `order_id` vs `quote_id` (the thread is client-scoped, so the business side is unchanged). **Scope:** order live pages are **view-only** (items + total + two-way chat) — no customer spec-edit / line-selection / accept / pay (those settings simply aren't set on orders, and `quote-public.js` relabels "quote"→"order" via `kind` + drops the accept CTA in `rail()`). **No schema work:** `orders.share_token`/`share_settings`/`viewed_at` + the unique index already existed (migration `20260604120000`), and `order_lines` already carries the customer flags. **Frontend:** `livelink.js` made entity-generic (`_llShareQuote('order')` now returns the order itself; new `_orderLinkPanel`; `_llEnsureLines`/`_sendLiveLink`/`_generateShareLink` take `kind`); `share.js` gains `_generateOrderShareLink` (mints token + `share_settings` on the order, no per-line snapshot) and `_openLiveOrderPage` now opens the order's own token. **Out of scope (follow-up):** deposit/card payment on order pages (needs `quote-pay` token support), customer spec-edit/selection on orders, order production status on the live page. **Deployed 2026-06-09**: `quote-public-get` v6 + `quote-messages` v4 (both `verify_jwt=false`). Verified end-to-end on prod: order 46 (ORD-SAMPLE, 3 lines) minted its own token; the deployed `quote-public-get` returns `kind:'order'`, `number:'ORD-SAMPLE'`, and the 3 `order_lines` (Base 600, Wall 600, Install & fit-off); `/q?t=…` renders **"Your order · ORD-SAMPLE"** with relabelled rail, no accept/pay CTA, and the floating Message launcher. - 2026-06-09 — **Quote/Order cards sync with live-link status (+ Supabase realtime)**. - 2026-06-09 — **Supabase Disk IO Budget warning — diagnosed as Nano-tier noise; added the 2 missing FK indexes on `customer_messages`.** Email from Supabase flagged `mhzneruvlfmhnsohfrdo`'s disk IO budget draining. Investigation (via Supabase MCP `pg_stat_statements` / `pg_stat_database` / `pg_statio_user_tables`): DB is 15 MB, **cluster cache-hit ratio = 100.00%** (1,628 disk reads vs 95M cache hits over 73 days), no app-side polling loop, the realtime publication has no public tables (so no logical-decoding WAL drag). The "300k SELECTs on stock_items/quotes/orders/clients" in pg_stat_statements are **73-day cumulative** (~4k/day each), normal for ~22 active users. Top WAL generators are auth-internal (`auth.refresh_tokens` UPDATE = 14 MB WAL over 73 days from hourly refresh × users), not anything app-controllable. **Verdict:** Nano-tier IO budget is conservative — a short write burst depleted the rolling budget; no fire. **Debounce audit:** all `oninput` per-keystroke writes (`cbUpdateField`, `_orderLineUpdate`, `_lineUpdate`) already debounce at 600ms through `_scheduleOrderLineUpsert` / `_scheduleLineUpsert` / `_cbScheduleAutosave` (`app.js:542,939`); non-debounced writes (`setStockQty`, `updateStockField`, `setOrderProdStart`, `_schedStepPriority`) fire on `onblur`/`onchange` only, one write per finished edit — **no change needed**. **What did ship:** migration `20260609010000_customer_messages_fk_indexes` (applied via MCP) adds `customer_messages_order_id_idx` + `customer_messages_quote_id_idx` — the 2 remaining unindexed-FK lints the advisor still showed after the 2026-05-18 FK-coverage pass. The 19 `unused_index` INFOs the advisor flagged were **deliberately left alone**: most are the FK covering indexes from `20260518150000` (kept to protect FK delete-cascade perf + future scaling once tables grow past seq-scan threshold) and the `*_tags_gin_idx` / `payments_*_idx` ones serve queries that haven't been heavily exercised yet. Advisor re-run confirms both `unindexed_foreign_keys` warnings cleared. **Recommended next step (not done):** upgrade compute add-on Nano → Micro (~$10/mo) when paid signups ramp — doubles the IO baseline and ends these notices.
- 2026-06-09 — **Stripe Connect customer payments — corrected the built charge model to the agreed Standard + direct-charge design (the shipped flow was losing money per transaction).** Pre-go-live test of `quote-pay`/`connect-onboard`/`quote-pay-webhook` + `src/connect.js`/`q.html` (all built + deployed during the overhaul) found two showstoppers: (1) it used **Express accounts + destination charges**, so per Stripe's docs the *platform* pays the ~2.9% processing fee while collecting only the application fee → **net loss on every card payment**, and destination charges carry cross-region limits that break the UK/US/CA/AU/NZ goal; (2) the **$100 fee cap was missing** and `STRIPE_PLATFORM_FEE_BPS` defaulted to **150 (1.5%)**, not the agreed **0.7%**. **Fix (revert to the locked model — confirmed with the founder):** `connect-onboard` now creates **`type:'standard'`** accounts (maker = merchant of record, carries dispute liability, pays Stripe's fee; Account Links hosted onboarding still works for Standard); `quote-pay` creates a **direct charge** (PaymentIntent on the connected account via the `{ stripeAccount }` option, no `transfer_data`) and returns `account_id`; `_shared/stripe.ts` defaults the fee to **70 bps (0.7%)** and adds a per-currency **~$100 cap** (`FEE_CAP_MINOR`: usd 10000/gbp 8000/eur 9000/cad 13500/aud 15000/nzd 16500); `src/quote-public.js` inits Stripe.js with `{ stripeAccount: pay.account_id }` so it can confirm the connected-account PaymentIntent. Verified against Stripe docs (direct charges: **connected account pays the processing fee**; Stripe.js **must** init with the connected account). `quote-pay` **v4** + `connect-onboard` **v4** redeployed ACTIVE via MCP; smoke green (OPTIONS 204; invalid-token POST → 404 `not_found`, proving the `_shared` bundle + Stripe client + DB all load). `npm run typecheck` clean. Commit `6711b61`; `quote-public.js` pushed 2026-06-09. **Pending before go-live:** (a) the `quote-pay-webhook` Stripe endpoint must be a **Connect** webhook (direct-charge `payment_intent.succeeded` fires on the connected account, not the platform) listening for `payment_intent.succeeded`/`payment_intent.payment_failed`; (b) confirm `STRIPE_PLATFORM_FEE_BPS=70` (or unset); (c) end-to-end test in test mode (onboard a Standard account → pay a `/q` deposit with a test card → verify the `payments` row, webhook, auto-created order, and the fee on the platform balance); (d) live-mode flip with the subscription Stripe S.9. `stripe_accounts`/`payments` had **0 rows** at fix time, so no Express accounts needed migrating.

- 2026-06-10 — **Live link: bank transfers (Stripe customer_balance) + `/payment-fees` page.** New per-quote `share_settings.allow_bank_transfer` toggle (livelink.js, persisted in share.js with the take_deposit element-missing fallback so the legacy popup can't wipe it). `quote-pay` keeps `automatic_payment_methods` (so Pay-by-bank still surfaces from the maker's own Stripe dashboard) and, when the toggle is on + currency supported (gbp/usd/eur+country/jpy/mxn), additionally creates a bare Customer ON the connected account and passes `payment_method_options.customer_balance` — Stripe requires both for push bank transfers; on rejection (capability not active) it retries card-only so the customer is never blocked. - 2026-06-10 — **Quote/order cards: one status language, status-wipe bug fixed, live link strictly optional.** The cards showed three overlapping status displays in two vocabularies (badge "Deposit paid" / pipeline "Approved" / meta stamp "✓ Accepted 2 Jun") and quietly fought a **critical autosave bug**: `saveQuoteEditor`/`saveOrderEditor` still read the long-removed `#pq-status`/`#po-status` selects via `_popupVal` (returns `''` for a missing element) and wrote **`status: ''` on every 600 ms autosave** — so the moment a maker touched a quote the customer had viewed/accepted/paid, the card fell back to "Draft" (and order pipelines lost their stage). That was the real source of the "statuses feel mixed up" report. **Fixes:** (1) both editors now PRESERVE the row's status — status is owned by the card pipeline + live-link events, not the editor; repaired the already-wiped prod rows via SQL (4 quotes — status inferred from `accepted_at`/`viewed_at`/`share_token` — and 5 orders → 'confirmed'). (2) **One vocabulary:** `QUOTE_STATUSES` last stage renamed Approved → **Accepted** ('approved' stays as a read alias labelled "Accepted"); `convertQuoteToOrder` and the pipeline write 'accepted'; the filter tab reads "Accepted (n)". (3) **Quote card = one status display:** the badge carries the granular label + date ("Viewed · 2 Jun", "Accepted · 2 Jun"); the duplicate `_llStamp` meta entry is gone; the pipeline's ACTIVE step shows the same granular word (Viewed/Deposit paid/Paid) so badge and pipeline can never disagree; a muted "Link live · not viewed yet" meta hint (`.qc-link-hint`) appears only when `share_token` exists and the link is unopened — makers who never share a link see a pure manual pipeline, nothing extra. (4) **Pipeline guard** (`setQuoteStatus` + `_applyQuoteStatus` + `_quoteCustomerFact`): same-stage clicks on a customer-driven status no-op (no silent viewed→sent downgrade); backward clicks from viewed/accepted/deposit_paid/paid open `_confirm` describing what the customer actually did ("The customer has paid a deposit on the live page. Move it back to Sent?") with a "payments aren't affected" note; manual-only statuses keep today's instant behaviour; forward clicks (e.g. phone-call acceptance) stay one-click. (5) **Order card separates dimensions:** the second look-alike badge (`_llChip`) is replaced by an outline `.oc-pay` pill in the META row — "✓ Paid in full" / "✓ Deposit paid · balance due" (green outline) / "Link live" (muted outline) — so production status (filled badge + pipeline, untouched) and money no longer read as two conflicting statuses. (6) **Dashboard:** Recent Quotes had its own 3-value ternary (the 2026-06-09 reconciliation missed it) — viewed/accepted/deposit_paid/paid rows showed "Draft"; now uses `_quoteStatusMeta`. Files: `src/quotes.js`, `src/orders.js`, `src/dashboard.js`, `styles.css`. `npm run typecheck` clean.

- 2026-06-10 — **Google sign-in (OAuth) added to the auth screen.** A "Continue with Google" button (official 4-colour G SVG, `.auth-oauth-btn`) sits above an "or" divider (`.auth-divider`) at the top of the auth card, before the email/password fields — visible in both signup and signin modes (one button serves both). New `signInWithGoogle()` (`src/app.js`, after `authSubmit`) calls `_sb.auth.signInWithOAuth({ provider: 'google', options: { redirectTo } })` with the same redirect target the email flow uses (`window.location.origin + (window._isDev ? '' : '/os')`). On success the page navigates to Google's consent screen; Google redirects back to `redirectTo`, the SDK's `detectSessionInUrl` exchanges the code, and the existing `onAuthStateChange` (SIGNED_IN) handler drives loadAllData/walkthrough/restore exactly like a password login — **no changes to the session handler were needed**. An `error` only returns synchronously if the redirect can't start (provider not configured / offline), surfaced in `#auth-msg`; a `google_signin_clicked` analytics event fires on click. **Decision/limitation:** OAuth signups can't carry the `marketing_opt_in` / first-touch `attribution` metadata that the email `signUp()` attaches — those come from Google's profile instead; acceptable since email prefs are managed in-app, but Google-originated accounts won't have paid-ads attribution stamped, and the marketing opt-in checkbox is bypassed. **Server-side config still required (dashboard, not code):** enable the Google provider in Supabase Auth → Providers with a Google Cloud OAuth client ID + secret; in Google Cloud Console set the authorized redirect URI to `https://mhzneruvlfmhnsohfrdo.supabase.co/auth/v1/callback`; ensure the prod `/os` URL + `http://localhost:3000` are in Supabase Auth → URL Configuration → Redirect URLs. Files: `index.html`, `src/app.js`, `styles.css`. `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview confirmed the button renders correctly and the handler is wired (full OAuth round-trip needs the dashboard config above to test).
- 2026-06-10 — **Marketing opt-in recovery for OAuth signups** (follow-up to the Google sign-in entry above). The email signup form's "send me cabinetry tips" checkbox writes `user_metadata.marketing_opt_in` at `signUp()` time, but OAuth/Google signups skip that form entirely and `signInWithOAuth` can't carry `data` metadata — so those accounts landed with the flag absent and **no way to ever opt in** (there's no Settings email-preferences toggle, and building one would need an unsubscribe endpoint that doesn't exist; opt-out is already handled by Resend's per-email unsubscribe link). New **`_maybePromptMarketingOptIn(session)`** (`src/auth.js`, beside `_syncMailingList`): a one-time, opt-in-only in-app consent card ("Stay in the loop?" → "No thanks" / "Yes, send tips", `popupFadeIn`/`popupSlideIn`, no new CSS) shown only to accounts whose `marketing_opt_in` is **not** a boolean (i.e. OAuth signups + any legacy pre-checkbox account); email signups always carry true/false and are skipped. "Yes" calls `_sb.auth.updateUser({ data: { marketing_opt_in: true } })` then re-reads the session and runs `_syncMailingList`; "No"/backdrop-dismiss records false / leaves it unset (default = not subscribed, no implied consent). A per-user `localStorage['pc_mkt_asked_<uid>']` flag is set the instant it's shown, so it's truly once-per-account-per-device regardless of the answer. **Hook** (`src/app.js` `onAuthStateChange` session branch, after `_restoreAppState`): `if (!_pendingPlanNow && !window._wtActive && …) _maybePromptMarketingOptIn(session)` — gated off the first-run walkthrough (`_wtActive`) and Checkout redirects so it never stacks on the tour; for a brand-new Google user the tour runs first and the prompt surfaces on a later load instead (where the flag is still unset). **Decision:** opt-in-only rather than a full preferences toggle — keeps consent explicit and GDPR/CAN-SPAM-clean and avoids half-building an unsubscribe path. `npm run typecheck` clean; dev preview verified the card renders and both gates block correctly (already-asked → no show; existing boolean preference → no show), no console errors.
- 2026-06-10 — **Orders → cabinet line editing UX pass.** The Orders→Builder round trip had four gaps: (1) the per-row “Open in Cabinet Builder” icon ignored WHICH cabinet was clicked — user landed in the Builder and had to re-find the cabinet among the cards; (2) “Done” left the user stranded in the Cabinet tab; (3) no Discard for orders (quotes had one); (4) the editing banner only rendered when the order had ≥1 cabinet — a zero-cabinet order had no banner, so no way back at all. **Fixes:** `editOrderInCB`/`editQuoteInCB` take an optional `lineId` and pre-select that cabinet (`cbEditingLineIdx`/`cbScratchpad` set before `renderCBPanel`; new `_cbRevealSelectedCabinet()` opens the mobile editor pane + scrolls form and highlighted card into view; `switchCBMainView('results')` runs FIRST since leaving library-edit clears the selection). New `_orderLineEditCabinetRow(idx)` (app.js) threads the clicked row’s id; order cabinet rows gain the same dblclick-to-edit as quotes; new `_liDblIgnore(event)` guard on BOTH tabs’ dblclick so double-click-to-select-text inside inputs/textareas (and the ✕ cell) no longer hijacks into the Builder. `finishEditingOrder()` now returns to the order (`switchSection('orders')` + `loadOrderIntoSidebar`); banner rebuilt — always rendered (empty state too), label leads with ORD-number, buttons are “Discard changes” + “← Back to order”; new `discardOrderEdits()` restores the entry snapshot by reusing `_syncCBLinesToOrder` then returns to the order. **Latent data-risk bugs fixed while in there:** `_exitClient_cabinet`/`_cbNewClient` cleared quote-editing state but NOT `cbEditingOrderId`/`pc_cb_editing_order_id` — after exiting, standalone autosaves still routed through `_syncCBLinesToOrder` and could wipe/corrupt that order’s cabinet lines; `_loadCBLinesFromDB` now restores an interrupted order-editing session from `pc_cb_editing_order_id` (was write-only — mid-edit reload silently fell back to the standalone workspace); the quote-restore branch now filters `line_kind='cabinet'` (it loaded item/stock rows as malformed cabinets, which the next sync re-inserted as duplicate cabinet lines). Files: `src/app.js`, `src/cabinet.js`, `src/cabinet-render.js` (the order editor's row HTML lives in app.js, so orders.js itself is untouched). `npm run typecheck` + `node --check` clean; rollup build not runnable in the work sandbox (mac-native binary).
- 2026-06-11 — **Cut layout "sometimes renders tiny" fixed with a width-watching ResizeObserver**. Root cause: `drawCanvas` fits the diagram to `wrap.clientWidth` at draw time with a 200px floor, the `renderLayout` retry guard only waits ~12 frames, and nothing re-rendered on size changes — so a layout rendered while the pane was hidden (other tab active when a cutlist loads/syncs) or mid-layout stuck at the tiny floor until the next manual re-render; window resizes/rotations also kept the stale scale. Fix (`src/cutlist.js`): `_clEnsureAreaObserver()` attaches one ResizeObserver to `#results-area` (armed from `renderResults`), `renderLayout` records the width it drew for in `_clDrawnW`, and the observer re-renders when the live width deviates by >24px. The 24px dead-band exceeds scrollbar width (~15-17px) so a re-render that toggles the scrollbar can't re-trigger itself; rAF-debounced. Verified in dev preview by driving the real render path: forced a draw at the 200px floor, widened the pane, observer redrew at the correct fit and `_clDrawnW` re-anchored (no oscillation). `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-06-11 — **Sentry triage → _db hardened against expired JWTs and insert races; Outlook noise filtered**. Three production Sentry issues, two real. (1) `JWT expired` 401 (PGRST303) silently dropped a `pieces` delete: the SDK's TOKEN_REFRESHED timer misses while a laptop sleeps / mobile tab freezes, so the in-memory token cache can hold a stale JWT. Fix in `src/db.js`: on any 401, `_db()` forces one `refreshSession()` (deduped across concurrent 401s via a shared in-flight promise), updates the cache, and replays the request once — headers rebuilt per attempt so the retry carries the fresh token. Safe to replay: a 401 means nothing committed. (2) `business_info` insert 409 after a "Failed to fetch": the request committed server-side, the client-side retry hit `business_info_user_id_key`. Root cause was the select-then-insert/update pattern (5 call sites: business.js ×3, migrate.js, walkthrough.js). Fix: native `upsert()` on `_DBBuilder` — POST with `Prefer: resolution=merge-duplicates` + `?on_conflict=` — and all 5 sites collapsed to single idempotent upserts. Partial payloads are safe because merge-duplicates only touches supplied columns and `name` has DB default `''` (the old "Need name (NOT NULL) — ensure baseline" insert padding was unnecessary and would have clobbered existing names if carried into upsert bodies — deliberately dropped). (3) `Object Not Found Matching Id:N, MethodName:update` — Microsoft Office/Outlook injected-script noise, added to `ignoreErrors` in main.js's Sentry init. `npm run typecheck` clean.
- 2026-06-11 — **Signup "check your email" dead ends fixed; thank-you panel replaces the missable green one-liner**. Diagnosis from auth logs + Resend delivery logs: (a) repeated signup of an already-confirmed email (`user_repeated_signup`) sends NO email by design (anti-enumeration: obfuscated user, empty `identities` array) yet the UI said "check your email" — the founder hit exactly this with adamdenney33@icloud.com (confirmed since 2026-05-17); (b) a real customer (mark@millersjoinery.co.uk) had 4 confirmation emails *delivered* by Resend but unclicked (spam suspected), retried into `over_email_send_rate_limit`, and all his links expired — `mailer_otp_exp` was only 3600s. Commit 78d9d08; typecheck clean; states verified live in dev preview incl. a real repeated-signup round-trip.
- 2026-06-11 — **App load performance pass: boot bundle 1.24 MB → 652 KB; boot data queries start before the scripts finish**. The /os boot was a strict waterfall (module bundle → 40 classic scripts → DOMContentLoaded → INITIAL_SESSION → ~9 render-gating queries → render) with jsPDF+autotable (~450 KB) and PostHog (~350 KB + recorder) shipped eagerly despite being needed late or never. Changes: (P.1) jsPDF lazy — `window._ensureJsPDF()` dynamic-imports jspdf then jspdf-autotable on first use (warmed post-`load`+3 s); the five `_build*PDF` builders await it (all call sites fire-and-forget, so async-ifying is safe) and keep their `!window.jspdf` guards. (P.2) PostHog dynamic-imported + init after `load`; `_identifyUser` stashes `window._pendingIdentify` when it races ahead, replayed by the init; `_resetAnalytics` clears it. (P.3) gtag/fbevents script *injection* deferred to `load` — the eager stubs queue calls, so boot-window conversions (signup) still flush. (P.4) Early boot fetch: main.js reads the stored session blob (same key as `_dbAuthToken`'s fallback, skipped if expires_at < now+30 s), fires the nine render-gating REST queries immediately (`window._earlyBoot`), with one retry on TypeError network failures (stale pooled socket killed all nine with ERR_CONNECTION_CLOSED in testing); `_earlyBootOr()` (db.js) consumes each slot once, guarded on `userId === _userId`, falling back to the identical `_db()` query on miss/HTTP-error/rejection — query shapes in main.js must mirror the consumer fallbacks. (P.5) `<link rel="preconnect" %VITE_SUPABASE_URL% crossorigin>` in index.html + q.html (Vite HTML env replacement). (P.6) favicons right-sized: 512 px/137 KB PNG → 64 px (3.9 KB) + 180 px apple-touch (18.5 KB), landing.html too. Verified in dev preview: 9/9 slots consumed on a signed-in reload (data/subscription/cbSettings identical), cross-user guard leaves stale slots untouched after a user switch, dead-refresh-token boot falls back cleanly to the auth screen, stock PDF exports with autotable patched on the lazy chunk; the empty `#biz-name` input observed during testing was confirmed pre-existing via a git-stash baseline. typecheck + build clean.
- 2026-06-11 — **Walkthrough auto-start gate scoped to the account, not the browser**. Report: "walkthrough isn't triggering for new users." Diagnosis from prod data + PostHog session replay: the first-run gate read `localStorage['pc_wt_state']`, which is per-BROWSER — any browser that ever dismissed the tour (as a guest in the pre-2026-06-07 demo era, which force-showed the tour to every logged-out visitor and persisted skips to localStorage, or under another account) suppressed the auto-tour for every account created on it afterwards. The founder's own prod test (workshop@bee9.co.uk, 17:57Z) reproduced it: confirm-link landing → no tour → had to launch it via Help → User Guide (visible in the session recording's autocapture trail). Desktop signups mskalla99/carina927 (both active 06-04, guest era) fit the same pattern. Of 13 recent no-tour signups, 9 were phones (tour is desktop-only by design; mobile advisory shows instead) and 1 (roland.marshall, "Desktop Mac" in PostHog) was actually an iPad — clicked `pc-mobile-notice-ok`; iPadOS requests desktop sites so analytics device-type lies. Fix: `_wtMaybeAutoStart` ignores the localStorage entry unless `ls.user_id === _userId` (guest-era/legacy entries have no user_id → ignored; `business_info.onboarding_state` remains the per-account cross-device gate, so properly-dismissed users aren't re-shown — and affected browsers self-heal on next sign-in); `_wtPersistState` stamps `user_id` into the localStorage copy (DB copy unchanged); `_applyBizInfoFromDB` resets `window._onboardingState = {}` when the account has no business_info row, so a previous account's in-memory state can't leak across a same-tab account switch. Verified in dev preview: planted guest-era `pc_wt_state` (no user_id) + never-onboarded account → tour fires; after skip (entry now user-stamped) → reload suppresses. typecheck clean.

- 2026-06-11 — **Tour pricing CTA suppressed for everyone with full Pro access — and the gate snapshotted before demo mode**. Request: "don't show the CTA screen for pro users." Two gaps: (1) the tour-end "Choose your plan" step and the skip → plan-picker hand-off gated on `isPro()` only, which excludes the automatic 14-day trial — so every fresh signup (always trialing, and labelled Pro in the UI) still ended the tour on pricing; the session CTA already excluded trialers, so the tour now matches that philosophy (`_hasProAccess`: paying OR trialing → no upsell; pricing waits for the trial-ending banner / weekly session CTA once it actually applies). (2) Deeper pre-existing bug: the tour borrows demo mode and the demo seed has `subscriptions: []`, so live `isPro()` reads false MID-TOUR even for paying users — the CTA-drop decision is made at render/skip time, meaning paying users re-running the tour still saw pricing. Fix: `_wtRunStart` snapshots `_wtNoUpsell = _hasProAccess()` over real data before flipping demo mode; `_wtLastIdx`/`_wtSkip` read the snapshot; `_wtStartCta` clears it (showing pricing is that overlay's whole job). Verified in dev preview on a paying account: mid-tour live `isPro()` false yet `_wtLastIdx()` drops the CTA step (stubbing the live gate mid-tour doesn't move it), skip produces no plan-picker hand-off, demo mode + real subscription restored after close. Guests/post-trial free users keep the CTA. Committed via selective hunk staging (`git apply --cached`) — the concurrent mobile-tour rework in the same file stays uncommitted worktree work. typecheck clean.
- 2026-06-11 — **Guided walkthrough runs on phones (and touch devices generally)**. Request: "make the walkthrough work on phones too." The tour was desktop-only by design — `_wtStart` returned early on touch and the static mobile notice showed instead. Changes (`src/walkthrough.js`, `styles.css`, `src/mobile-notice.js` comment): touch gate removed; each step declares `mv: 'list'|'editor'` and the tour drives `body[data-mv]` (mobile-nav.js) to the pane holding its target — applied AFTER the pre-click since card handlers call `_mvShowEditor` and `switchSection` resets to list; on ≤760px the tooltip pins sheet-style to the top/bottom screen edge away from the spotlight centre (side-anchoring can't fit beside full-width targets; arrow dir reuses the existing top/bottom math); touch devices get a fingertip tap-dot pointer instead of the mouse-arrow SVG (`#wt-cursor .wt-tap-dot`, tip = circle centre) plus swipe left/right navigation on the overlay (passive listeners, 60px floor + 1.5× dx:dy ratio so CTA scrolling and taps never navigate); device-aware copy via `bodyTouch` (welcome "arrow keys" → "swipe left or tap Next"; touch = `_pcIsTouchDevice`, so iPads get it too) and `bodyNarrow` (schedule gantt-bars copy → agenda copy; narrow = `_mvIsMobile`). Pre-clicks hardened: `preClickCard` is now awaited via `_wtWaitFor` (visible+sized) before clicking instead of a blind sync `querySelector().click()` — the Cut List Library grid renders async, and its synchronous "Loading…" placeholder div taught us the selector must be `#cl-lib-grid > div[onclick]`; the Cut List step now pre-opens a demo cut list from the library so the spotlit `.cl-left` shows populated sheet/piece tables on ALL form factors (previously the 26→10-step trim left it spotlighting the "no cut list open" gate). `_wtMaybeAutoStart` shows the mobile notice only when the full tour is NOT auto-starting (the tour is the welcome; returning users keep the once-per-session notice). CSS: CTA plan picker stacks to one column ≤480px (li min-height released), tour buttons ≥42px on coarse pointers. Verified in dev preview at 390×844 with forced touch: all 10 steps land on the right pane (list/editor trail confirmed), library card pre-click fires (`OPEN:` hook), sheet tooltip flips top/bottom per target half, swipe-back works and a mostly-vertical drag doesn't navigate; desktop 1280×800 re-verified unchanged (anchored tooltips, arrow cursor, keyboard copy, cut-list step now opens real data there too). typecheck clean. WT_VERSION deliberately NOT bumped — mobile users never dismissed the tour (it never ran there), and desktop users have nothing new to learn.
- 2026-06-11 — **Quote line-item autosave 400 fixed — second `schedule_hours: null` write path**. Report: "SAVE FAILED · RETRY" pill when saving a line item on prod. API log: `PATCH /quote_lines?id=eq.776` → 400; postgres log: 23502 null in `schedule_hours` (NOT NULL default 0). The Sentry JAVASCRIPT-6 fix guarded `saveQuoteEditor` (quotes.js) but missed the debounced per-line autosave `_scheduleLineUpsert` (app.js), which still sent `row.schedule_hours ?? null` — and a freshly added line has no local `schedule_hours` (the `_lineAdd`/`_qAddStockLineFromLibrary` insert literals omit it; only `id` is copied back from the insert), so the first keystroke on a new "+ Item"/stock-library line 400'd every autosave AND every RETRY (the retry closure re-sends the same null); name/qty/price edits were silently unsaved until a full editor save ran. Fix: `?? 0` in `_scheduleLineUpsert` (mirrors the saveQuoteEditor guard) + `schedule_hours: 0` seeded into both insert literals so local rows mirror the DB row. Order twin (`_scheduleOrderLineUpsert` `?? null`) deliberately untouched — `order_lines.schedule_hours` is nullable. Verification: preview session was signed out, so the replay ran at the SQL layer — stuck prod row 776 (name still '', updated_at == created_at, proving the PATCH never landed) updated with exactly the fixed payload, succeeding and healing the user's line; served-source check confirmed Vite ships the guard. typecheck clean.
- 2026-06-11 — **Pro subscribe/portal/pricing CORS preflight failure fixed — `apikey` header was never allow-listed**. Report: clicking any paid plan toasted "Load failed (mhzneruvlfmhnsohfrdo.supabase.co)" (Safari's TypeError for a failed fetch; the host suffix is Safari's, not ours — the string exists nowhere in the repo). Edge logs showed ZERO stripe-checkout requests (not even OPTIONS) while connect-status traffic flowed fine: the request died browser-side. Root cause: commit 888d1ec (2026-06-09, in-memory-token fix) switched stripe.js's three edge calls to raw `fetch` and added an `apikey` header, but stripe-checkout/stripe-portal/stripe-subscription carry hand-rolled inline CORS (predating `_shared/cors.ts`) allowing only `authorization, content-type` — so every preflight failed and Checkout has been unreachable in prod since June 9. Fix: widened all three inline lists to `authorization, content-type, apikey, x-client-info` (matching `_shared/cors.ts`); redeployed via CLI preserving each function's verify_jwt (checkout v27 + portal v20 `--no-verify-jwt`; subscription v13 verify_jwt=true — the blanket "deploy with --no-verify-jwt" memory is wrong for this one). Verified live: OPTIONS preflight from procabinet.app origin now returns the full allow-list on all three, and a POST carrying `apikey` reaches function code (401 "Invalid auth token" for a fake bearer, i.e. past CORS). Inline lists deliberately NOT refactored onto `_shared/cors.ts` mid-incident — minimal diff on live billing functions.
- 2026-06-11 — **Boot data loaded twice on every page load — fixed with a per-user guard in the auth handler (perf pass P.7)**. User report: "data takes ~15 s to load" despite the P.1–P.6 pass. Production waterfall (Playwright + Performance API on procabinet.app/os, signed in) showed the early-boot queries landing by ~0.7 s — then the ENTIRE load repeating at ~1.6 s: supabase-js emits INITIAL_SESSION and then SIGNED_IN for the same stored session on every page load (plus SIGNED_IN on tab refocus and TOKEN_REFRESHED hourly), `onAuthStateChange` ran the full `loadAllData()` + `_loadCabinetTemplatesFromDB()` on each, and supabase-js serializes async callbacks — so the two full loads ran back-to-back (~38 REST requests; the duplicate also wiped every `_lines`/`_totals` cache, re-hydrating and re-rendering everything). On a slow connection that serialized double load is the ~15 s. Fix: `_bootLoadedUserId` — the session branch bails early when `session.user.id` matches the already-loaded user (token cache is updated before the guard; realtime keeps quotes/orders live), cleared on the no-session branch so sign-out → sign-in reloads. Walkthrough exit is unaffected (it calls `loadAllData()` directly). Deliberate trade: tab-refocus SIGNED_IN no longer re-pulls cross-device edits for stock/clients/settings (quotes/orders still sync via realtime). DB exonerated first: advisors clean, biggest table 116 rows, no query > 50 ms mean. Dev-verified: every boot table fetched exactly once (18 vs 38 requests). typecheck clean.
- 2026-06-12 — **Pre-boot nav tap ReferenceError fixed (Sentry JAVASCRIPT-D) — stub + boot replay**. Prod event: iPhone Safari user tapped the Cut List nav tab on /os/ and got `ReferenceError: Can't find variable: switchSection` — the shell is plain HTML, the nav is tappable while the ~38 deferred classic scripts download, and `switchSection` lives 25th in the chain (settings.js). Fix: a one-line inline stub in the index.html head (`window.switchSection = n => window._preBootSection = n`) so the inline onclick always resolves; settings.js's top-level function declaration overwrites the stub at execute time (classic-script global binding semantics), and `restoreAppState` (persist.js) replays the stashed tap at boot with priority over the persisted last-section restore — the tap is honored, not just swallowed. Signed-out taps stash harmlessly (no boot → no replay). Verified in dev preview: stub present in served head, real switchSection after load, simulated stash + `_restoreAppState()` lands on Cut List and clears the stash. typecheck clean.
- 2026-06-12 — **Mobile tour: Finish no longer "sticks"; sheet tooltip always bottom-pinned**. Founder's phone test surfaced two issues with the 2026-06-11 mobile walkthrough. (1) Tapping Finish appeared to hang: `_wtClose` deliberately awaited the demo→real `loadAllData()` restore BEFORE removing the overlay (the no-demo-flash rule), so on a phone connection the frozen spotlight/tooltip sat there for seconds — unbounded if a fetch stalled. Fix: the tour chrome (tooltip/spotlight/cursor/dropdowns) is stripped the moment close starts and the dim mask stays up with a `.wt-restore` "Loading your data…" spinner pill, so the tap visibly responds, demo content still never flashes, and the restore is capped at 12 s via `Promise.race` (a stalled fetch can't trap the user; late responses render when they land). Guests/CTA-only closes are untouched (no `_wtTempDemo` → immediate teardown, no pill). (2) The ≤760px sheet tooltip flipped to the TOP edge when the target's centre sat in the bottom half — covering exactly the pane headers/names/first-fields the step was describing. Now always bottom-pinned (`dir='bottom'`, arrow on the sheet's top edge); panes carry their key info at the top, and `scrollIntoView(block:'center')` keeps the target's upper half clear of the sheet. Verified in dev preview at 390×844 on the real signed-in account (Pro → 9-step tour ending on Dashboard "Finish", the reported path): every spot step's tooltip bottomGap=14, and with `loadAllData` wrapped in a 3 s delay the Finish tap removed tooltip/spot/cursor and showed the pill within ~250 ms, then teardown landed with real data restored, demo off, dashboard active. typecheck clean, no console errors.

- 2026-06-12 — **Cancelled payment no longer accepts the quote — acceptance moved to post-payment, webhook backfills.** Founder repro on QUO-0001: "Accept & pay" → close the card sheet → quote locked as accepted (status `accepted`, `accepted_at` stamped, snapshot stored) with £0 taken — `payDeposit()` called `recordAccept()` right after the PaymentIntent was created, before the customer ever saw the card form. Fix across three files: (1) quote-public.js records acceptance only after `confirmPayment` resolves without error (covers card success, `processing`, and bank-transfer-committed — bankPending/processing states already stamped `accepted_at` locally, so semantics unchanged), plus in `boot()`'s `redirect_status` branch since redirect methods (Pay by bank) never return from `confirmPayment`; `recordAccept` gains an accepted guard. (2) quote-pay-webhook v13 backfills `accepted_at` (`?? now`) on `payment_intent.succeeded` so a tab closed mid-flow can't leave a paid quote unaccepted/editable (accepted_at is the public-page edit lock). (3) quote-public-update v15's accept action no longer downgrades `deposit_paid`/`paid` → `accepted` when the webhook wins the race (snapshot is skipped on 409 — informational only, order rebuilds from lines server-side). `quote-pay` never gated on accepted_at, so pay-after-accept still works. Verified on the live flow (local fixed JS + prod functions, quote 91 reset first): sheet open with real Stripe element mounted → DB still `viewed/null`; cancel + reload → "Awaiting your approval" with the pay button live, DB untouched. Success path not live-tested (would charge a real card); it's the same accept call relocated + the deployed webhook backfill. Stray artifacts of the bug: one `pending` payments row per abandoned sheet (pre-existing behaviour, PIs expire server-side).
- 2026-06-12 — **Boot loading screen — the app no longer opens as an empty shell while data loads.** New `#boot-loader` overlay (logo + spinner + "Loading your workspace…") in `index.html`, visible from first paint; cleared by `window._hideBootLoader()`. Decisions: helper + 15s failsafe defined in the head pre-boot inline script (NOT a deferred src file) so the overlay can never trap the user even if a later script fails to load; hide points are `_showAuth()` (signed-out destination) and a `finally` around `await loadAllData()` (panels rendered — or load threw); z-index 10000 = above auth screen (9999) and popups (8000, so the PASSWORD_RECOVERY popup surfaces only after load), below toasts (99999); saved `pcDark` theme now pre-applied in the same head script (try/catch for storage-blocked in-app browsers) so dark-mode users don't get a light flash — settings.js still owns the theme and re-applies it. `npm run typecheck` clean.
